VGreen Party Hypocrites Justify Support for Electoral Finance Bill
p66
sg6
Vhttp://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/12/green-party-hypocrites-justify-support.html
p67
sg8
(lp68
sg10
VThe Green Party is worried. Stung by recent low polling, they've figured out that its probably related to their support for Labour's hugely unpopular Electoral Finance Bill.<br /><br />Here's some extracts from a mass email sent out in the name of their <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/05/is-russel-norman-being-little.html">formerly?Trotskyist co-leader Russel Norman </a>and their <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/11/not-so-happy-valley-campers-green-party.html">anarchist MP, Metiria Turei</a>.<br /><br />Some comment from me in bold.<br /><br /><em>Protecting free speech and fairer elections<br />  <br />Please forward this email to as many people as you can to get the truth out there.<br />  <br />Many of you will have seen media reports and even paid advertising about the Electoral Finance Bill. Given the controversy around this Bill, we thought it was important that we wrote to you directly to explain the Green position.<br /> <br />The Electoral Finance Bill deals with one of the most important issues in our democracy - controls on the financing of election campaigns to protect the integrity of the ballot from the inequality of the wallet.</em><br /> <br /><em>The Greens have had many concerns about this Bill but we have chosen to work constructively with all parties. Our aim has been to improve the laws around campaign finance so that we<br />- have a fairer election system,<br />- ensure a more level playing field, and<br />- limit the corrupting influence of large secret donations on political parties.<br /> <br />The opponents of campaign finance reform<br /> <br />However, much of the publicity that has surrounded this Bill has been one-sided and, in fact, some has even been funded by wealthy donors who want the law to stay the same. They are trying to frighten New Zealanders by saying the Bill impacts on freedom of speech \u2013 this is not true.</em><br /><br /><strong>A little dig at private individual John Boscawen, who has funded the anti EFB campaign largely out of his own pocket.</strong><br /> <br /><em>Some media organisations have also been running an active and misleading campaign against the Bill. Journalists have contacted us to tell us that they oppose the misleading editorial line of their papers, but it is very difficult for them to get their views across.</em> <br /><br /><strong>Paranoia runs deep.</strong><br /><br /><em>So what does the Bill do (and what doesn't it do)?<br /> <br />* The Bill does not restrict freedom of speech \u2013 it just caps election campaign spending.<br />* Any person or group can purchase as much issue advertising as they want at any time.<br />* The Bill only places limits on how much election advertising political parties and others can purchase in an election year. That limit is $2.4m for political parties and $120,000 for any other group or individual.<br />* Any group or individual who purchases more than $12,000 in election ads must register with the Electoral Commission so there is transparency about who is involved in the election campaign.</em><br /><br /><strong>All this clearly inhibits free speech. One point the Greens fail to address is the real reasons donors should be able to remain anonymous-political revenge.<br /><br />We have anonymous voting, so that no voter need feel intimidated by a potentially vindictive victor. <br /><br />Many businesses in mixed economy New Zealand rely on government contracts for at least part of their income. Some business people already feel too intimidated to overtly support anti government parties. This bill will make that worse, potentially reducing funding for pro-business parties-a point I'm sure that was not overlooked by the bill's leftist framers.</strong><br /><br /><em>The spending caps exist to stop parties spending millions on campaigning and then needing to raise those millions in donations. Once parties rely on millions in donations they become heavily influenced by those who provide the money. The caps on political parties only work if there are caps on spending by other groups, otherwise the money goes into parallel campaigns.</em><br /><br /><strong>Having to raise money from donors-large or small, makes parties more responsive to the public. It engenders some humility. The alternative is open or covert state funding of political parties. This makes parties even less connected to the public and even more arrogant than they are now. </strong> <br /><br /><em>Closing the loopholes<br /> <br />Those who are most strongly opposed to the Bill took advantage of two major loopholes in our electoral financing regime in 2005.<br /> <br />- The first loophole enabled an organisation to work with a political party to run an almost identical campaign - known as parallel campaigning. This meant that the spending of the organisation was not capped even though it was a planned party election campaign.</em><br /><br /><strong>A clear dig at the Exclusive Brethren. Why should private individuals not be able to support anyone they like with their own tax paid cash?</strong><br /><br /><strong>Greenpeace has been supporting Green Party campaigns for years-using tax deductible donations, even though Greenpeace is a clearly political organisation and has openly advised against voting National in the past.</strong><br /> <br /><em>- The second loophole allowed for millions of dollars to be given to political parties without the public knowing who gave that money. Both the USA and Australian electoral systems have suffered from the corruption that arises from the secret funding of political parties.</em><br /><br /><strong>All paranoid speculation stated as fact. The New Zealand left has enjoyed huge financial and "volunteer" labour contributions from unions, Greenpeace etc, over many years. </strong> <br /><br /><em>The Greens are proud to assist in the closing of those two loopholes. This work will protect our electoral system from the threats of corruption that other similar democracies face.<br /> <br />It's far from perfect<br /> <br />However, we still have some outstanding issues with the Bill and with the process for these electoral law reforms. We are still pursing the option of a citizens' assembly which would allow for a number of randomly selected citizens to consider the issues of electoral finance and to find the best system for New Zealand. This system has been used successfully in Canada and we believe that the people of New Zealand should be able to make these decisions.<br /> <br />We have not achieved the ban on anonymous donations over $1000 that is our policy. However we have severely restricted the anonymous donations that can be received by both a third party and a political party. This is a major change in the law and goes someway towards a system that is open about who is funding political campaigns.<br /> <br />Changes the Greens achieved in the Bill<br /> <br />In summary, the Greens have made the following amendments:<br /> <br />Amendments to protect freedom of speech<br /> <br />1. Alter the definition of election advertising to protect issues advertising. This means that individuals and groups will be free to campaign on the issues that are important to them, regardless of whether one or more parties is also campaigning on the same issue. The Greens come from a campaigning background and we were determined to protect the right of groups to continue to campaign. For example, Greenpeace can continue to campaign against whaling, even though it is a campaign the Green Party has a profile on.</em><br /><br /><strong>Has Greenpeace, which has been extremely worried about this bill had a word in the Green Party's ear. No that couldn't possibly be. The Green Party is completely opposed to any covert influence on the electoral system.</strong><br /> <br /><em>2. Remove the requirement for a statutory declaration for spending less than the threshold. This means that people or groups don't have to sign a statutory declaration every time they spend money under the threshold for listing as a third party. It was an unnecessary burden that performed no useful function.<br /> <br />3. Lift the cap on election spending by non-party groups from $60,000 to $120,000. Many groups and individuals engage in election advertising during campaign year. This advertising encourages voters to support parties that adopt certain policy positions. The Bill as introduced limited this spending to $60,000. The Greens have supported amendments that increase this limit to $120,000, 5% of the $2.4m party limit and twice that originally proposed.<br /> <br />4. Lift the spending limit at which a group must list as a third party from $5000 to $12,000. This was important because many groups and people engage in election advertising through pamphlets, newsletters or community newspaper adverts. These ordinary election activities should not require a person or group to have to list as a third party where the spending is under $12,000.<br /> <br />5. Enable under 18 year olds and permanent residents to be able to list as a third party. We fought for the inclusion of this because it is a breach of the rights of a citizen to be prevented from engaging in election advertising activities simply because they are not old enough to vote. This change also means that groups will not be excluded from listing as a third party simply because one member is under 18 years old.<br /> <br />6. Protect donations to groups that are not for election purposes. This means that groups that register as third party participants in the election will not have to declare any donations that are not specifically for election purposes.<br />Groups are entitled to raise and collect money for their regular activities without interference. Only donations given specifically for electioneering will need to be disclosed.<br /> <br />Amendment to restrict anonymous donations<br /> <br />7. Severely restrict anonymous donations to political and third parties. The Greens insisted on an anonymous donations regime that will restrict Labour and National's ability to raise money through anonymous donations. Our policy is that all donations over $1000 should be identified as to the true source \u2013 they shouldn't be listed as anonymous nor should they be hidden behind secret trusts.<br /> <br />In negotiations over this bill we have made progress towards achieving our policy by introducing a system that will limit political parties to a total anonymous donations income, for donations over $1000, of 10% of their spending cap over the three year electoral cycle \u2013 this would cut Labour's anonymous donations income by at least half and National's secret trust income by about 90%. Labour and National don't like it but we make no apologies for this.</em><br /><br /><strong>Labour will make up the shortfall by giving more money to the unions, (which will launder it back to Labour) and by milking the state tit. National will be forced to support state funding of political parties. Any parties, like ACT, that are vehemently opposed to state funding will be disadvantaged.</strong> <br /><br /><em>In addition the money must be passed via the Electoral Commission to distance the parties from the process and donors must identify themselves to the Electoral Commission and give an assurance that they are not telling the parties about the donation on the sly. There is a limit of $36,000 on how much any one donor can give to a political party via this mechanism.<br /> <br />Best wishes<br /> <br />Metiria and Russel<br /> <br />Metiria is the Green MP responsible for the Bill in the House; Russel is Spokesperson on Electoral Matters.</em><br /><br /><strong>No doubt Greenpeace will be very happy about all their friends, the Green Party has done for them.</strong>

VPope Benedict's message on climate change and world peace
p142
sg6
Vhttp://nzconservative.blogspot.com/2007/12/pope-benedicts-message-on-climate.html
p143
sg8
(lp144
sg10
VLooks like the Pope has caused a bit of a storm with a whole range of people.  Andrei has <a href="http://briefingroom.typepad.com/the_briefing_room/2007/12/climate-change.html">a good post up on the details</a>.  Not PC is <a href="http://pc.blogspot.com/2007/12/sense-and-non-sense-from-would-be-world.html">a little surprised</a>, but then he puts it all down to the advisers the Pope must have.<br /><br />I'd just like to highlight a couple of statements that stood out to me.<br /><blockquote>... fears over man-made emissions melting the ice caps and causing a wave of unprecedented disasters were nothing more than <span>scare-mongering</span>.<br /><br />The German-born Pontiff said that while some concerns may be valid it was vital that the international community <span>based its policies on science rather than the dogma of the environmentalist movement</span>.</blockquote><span id="fullpost">This has been my position on climate change all along - I'm so glad I don't need to reconsider!<br /><blockquote>... the world needed to care for the environment but <span>not </span>to the point where the <span>welfare of animals and plants</span> was given a <span>greater priority</span> than that of mankind.</blockquote>Yes!  All those people that are so worried about whales or giant snails - are they at all perturbed by tiny human babies being sucked out of their mother's wombs?  Related to that, this Sunday marks 400,000 tiny human lives taken by abortion in NZ in the last 30 years.<br /><blockquote>"The human community cannot do without the service provided by the family. Where can young people gradually learn to savor the genuine 'taste\u201A' of peace better than in the original 'nest\u201A' which nature prepares for them."<br /><br />...<br /><br />"Whoever, even unknowingly, circumvents the institution of the family undermines peace in the entire community, national and international, since he weakens what is in effect the primary agency of peace. This point merits special reflection: Everything that serves to weaken the family based on the marriage of a man and a woman constitutes an objective obstacle on the road to peace."</blockquote>It has often been asked why gay marriage threatens traditional marriage.  As if someone else's marriage could threaten another's.  But the threat is not so much direct as indirect.  Once the notion of marriage, all it entails, all it's responsibilities are changed, marriage is weakened.  If it is considered that marriage is temporary, until one "partner" falls out of love, then marriage is weakened, and the children's ability to form life long relationships is weakened, as they've never seen how a life long relationship works.  If any man and his dog can get married, then marriage becomes a joke, something no one really needs or aspires to.  Yet marriage is fundamentally necessary in raising children and instilling values.  Without that, everything falls apart.  And we can see that happening quite clearly in NZ.<br /><br />Related Links: <a href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/pages/live/articles/news/worldnews.html?in_article_id=501316&amp;in_page_id=1811">Daily Mail</a>, <a href="http://www.nysun.com/article/67983?page_no=3">New York Sun</a><br /></span>

V<ul>\u000A<li><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&amp;objectid=10480731">"Cafe fined for allowing smoking," 6th December 2007, NZ Herald</a></li>\u000A</ul>\u000A<blockquote><p>\u000APopular Wellington cafe Fidel's has been fined $600 for allowing smoking on-site... VThe toddler has discovered Christmas carols.<br /><br />This is great: her health issues mean she is way behind in her language and related social skills. But she's always responded well to music and she has picked up about half a dozen Christmas carols in the space of a week.<br /><br />So we've been woken (she's like her dad, an early riser: I'd assumed I would welcome this but I now see the downside) several mornings with 'We Wish You a Merry Christmas' 'Good King Wencelas' or a sort of  blend of 'Hark the Herald Angels' and 'Once in Royal David's City'.<br /><br />Or 'We Three Kings' (also known as ' Star of Wonder'.)<br /><br />Now, this last one is kind of interesting. I don't know the 'proper' words to it: I only know the Fred Dagg version, which was done way back in 197omumble.<br /><br />I've been running this past a lot of people - of, I guess, a broadly similar age to myself -  and first I get a quizzical look as they try to think of what the real words are. Then they say, 'yeah, me too...'<br /><br />So, herewith, both versions<br /><br /><div><span>Fred Dagg</span><br /><span></span><br />We three kings of Orient are<br />One on a tractor, two in a car<br />One on a scooter tooting a hooter<br />Following yonder star.<br /><br />Ooh - Ooooh....<br /><br />Star of wonder<br />Star of light<br />Star of beauty, she'll be right<br />Star of glory, that's the story<br />Following yonder star.<br /><br /><div>Somewhat surprisingly, no-one has Youtubed this yet. There was a video clip done of it at the time but perhaps it has long since been shredded.<br /><br /></div><br /><span>The Original Version</span><br /><span></span></div><br /><br /><div>We three kings of Orient are<br />Bearing gifts we traverse afar<br />Field and fountain, moor and mountain<br />Following yonder star<br /><br />O Star of wonder, star of night<br />Star with royal beauty bright<br />Westward leading, still proceeding<br />Guide us to thy Perfect Light<br /></div><br /><br />There's a heap of other verses, but we don't need to labour the point, I feel.<br /><br /><span><span></span><br /></span><span><span><span><br /><br /></span></span></span>

VAntarctic Story
p231
sg6
Vhttp://silentrunning.tv/?p=2566
p232

(lp233

V<p>If New Zealand is a dagger thrusting at the heart of Antarctica then Christchurch is that knife-point. This is the base-camp for everyone going on down to mix it with the penguins. Always has been. From Falcon Scott and Amundson, and on. Not for nothing we have Scott's statue in town, nor that we've got the International Antarctic Center.</p>\u000A<p>And now we're base-camp for another great civilising venture.</p>\u000A<p align="center"><img id="image2565" title="airbus.jpg" alt="airbus.jpg" src="http://silentrunning.tv/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/airbus.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p align="center"><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4322766a12.html">http://www.stuff.co.nz/4322766a12.html</a></p>\u000A<p>Just one problem...</p>\u000A<blockquote><p>Australia has scored an Antarctic coup by successfully landing a commercial airliner at its polar base.</p>\u000A<p>Its success has major implications for the Christchurch based polar operation which each summer despatches military aircraft southward.</p></blockquote>\u000A<p>Yes. Those bloody Australians are doing it! Not us! This is worse than that time they stuck an Australian flag on that huge break-away ice burg off the coast of Otago!</p>\u000A<p>Christchurch is still the penultimate lilly pad. Flippin' dingo-owners have dropped a crikey in the tucker bag and nailed the goanna, but!</p>\u000A<p>Why aren't Kiwis leading the way on this one!!? I'll tell you why: Erebus. We crashed into it.</p>\u000A<p>A great big Mountain, an active volcano, and on the subcontinent to end all subcontinents. Something to see. As a great achievement of civilisation and man's grasp of nature, Air New Zealand used to fly tourists to Erebus for a look, then home again. Used to.</p>\u000A<p>In 1979 one such flight went horribly wrong. The crash scarred Erebus a little, but New Zealand a lot. All died. I had dinner with a bloke the other day and it came up that he was mates with one of those sent down to collect the corpses- he was severely effected. Back then (apart from 6mth olds like me) most everyone in NZ was related to, or knew someone, involved. As usual, when something goes wrong in New Zealand, we respond with a knee-jerk. No more flights to Erebus.</p>\u000A<p>Of course, what a proper capitalist country would do would be to get back on the horse.</p>\u000A<p>Australia, 28years latter, has done. It's not on their national psyche as it is ours, and thus they have trumped us. Again.\u000A</p>

VWrong result, wrong excuses, but legally mainstream reasoning on McNamara parole.
p252
sg6
Vhttp://www.stephenfranks.co.nz/?p=231
p253
sg8
(lp254
sg10
V<p>The Parole Board has just released a legally defensible, but morally wrong decision to let Peter McNamara out on parole after Christmas. Previously they made a <a target="_blank" href="http://www.paroleboard.govt.nz/media-and-publications/decisions/mcnamara-peter-mana-28-08-07.html" title="Parole Board decision">morally correct but illogical decision</a> to  turn down his application for home detention. They kept him in prison for a 1989 rape until now, when he's served a bit over 2 years 6 months of the 7-year sentence.</p>\u000A<p>The issue was whether they could take into account the outrageousness of gutting a 7 year sentence, to refuse to release him, when he is not a threat to anyone in the community. They faced an impossible task. The government tried to write the law to obscure what they were telling the Board, but the original intention was clear -"<em>it's not your business to worry about justice, you must let them out if you feel they are not a risk. If that makes a mockery of sentencing, and insults the victims, that's not your problem".</em></p>\u000A<p>Select Committee changes confounded that simplicity. For example the Board is told to consider the interests of victims, but Labour and the Greens would not allow those interests to be defined or give them equal weight with the instruction to release. I do not apologise for the resulting confusion.</p>\u000A<p>The Board is bound by the Court of Appeal's decision in Reid et al v New Zealand Parole Board (CA 247/05) ...<em>"although considerations of general deterrence are relevant when setting the nominal sentence and minimum periods of imprisonment and in determining whether to grant leave to apply for home detention, they are not relevant when the Parole Board is considering applications for release on parole or home detention".</em></p>\u000A<p><font size="2">In the decision on home detention the Board raised something called 'personal deterrence' and the victim's views, and even the public concern for victims expressed in the 92% Withers petition for tougher sentencing to justify holding a man that nobody thinks will offend again.</font><font size="2">They were morally right, but the reasoning was crap.</font><font size="2">Now their reasoning is better but the outcome is wrong.</p>\u000A<p>There are arguments to get around the Court of Appeal decision. They could have said "<em>we are not letting you out because it would make a mockery of justice. If people believe that court-ordered sentences are nonsense, they will feel that crime does pay, that honesty is not the best policy, that only mugs obey the law. That loss of confidence in justice, in the basic fairness of the law is very dangerous to everyone in the community."</em></p>\u000A<p>They could have set it out like this (for appeal proofing purposes) " <em>we are not trying to deter bad people, we are trying to reassure good people - to reassure them that it is worth assisting the Police, that it is correct to teach your children that crime will not pay, to show that the long arm of the law will ensure the price of crime is paid".</em></p>\u000A<p>They could have had good academic support. The safety of the community is dictated by the crime rate, not individual release decisions. And there is strong evidence that the crime rate is most affected by what people believe is the prevailing norm. If it is generally not done to break the rules - few do. People on the crime margin are sensitive to what appears to be the prevailing climate. They should be the preoccupation of the system. Every element should be driven by its influence on those who could offend but do not (in low crime societies), or can and do (in high crime societies). Our religious forebears might have expressed it simply - the system should focus on those in temptation, not those who've made the decision to be bad.</p>\u000A<p>Instead ours is all focussed on those who have offended, and the vain task of turning them around once they have crossed the threshold. The international evidence says it is a waste of time.</p>\u000A<p>"Broken windows" is the shorthand name for the theory which underlay New York's dramatic crime turn-around. The police stopped concentrating on serious crime. Instead they enforced all the small laws (like those against shoplifting and begging, and leaping the turnstiles in subways, even jaywalking and littering. They insisted that graffiti be cleaned up immediately because it sent the message that rules do not apply. The result, in short order, was to cut every category of serious crime by more than 70% and the murder rate by 80% (in some years parts of provincial New Zealand now have a higher murder rate).</p>\u000A<p>Even if they could not step outside the NZ establishment orthodoxy enough to raise those arguments I would have respected the Parole Board much more if they'd simply said to the government in the decision- "<em>Change the unjust law. We are going to find every way we can not to apply it the way you want. We are sick of carrying the can for your dishonest criminal statutes. We will not tell the victim who is comforted by a 7 year sentence that sentencing is a calculated lie, a charade to be undone by parole</em>" .</p>\u000A<p>There is nothing unprecedented in a court or judicial body telling the poor litigants not to blame them when a law does not work, and asking Parliament to fix it.</p>\u000A<p>I have often excused the Parole Board for sad cases because the law is bad. But I've been too charitable. They've never called for reform.</p>\u000A<p>At the Graeme Burton enquiry they should have said <em>" We are ashamed of ourselves. There have been too many Graeme Burtons. We have not spoken out about the impossible law we are applying. From now on we will".</em></p>\u000A<p>In this McNamara decision they initially told a few insiders who can understand the code- <em>"this law is hopeless, and we are now going to ignore it". </em> Now I would not let them out of the dock.</p>\u000A<p>I hope this is appealed.</p>\u000A<p></font></p>

VWhen is a constitution not a constitution?
p261
sg6
Vhttp://briefingroom.typepad.com/the_briefing_room/2007/12/when-is-a-const.html
p262
sg8
(lp263
sg10
V<div><p>Answer: <a href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/7141651.stm">When it is a treaty</a>.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The ill fated EU constitution that was resoundedly rejected by European voters&nbsp; has reappeared in a reduced form and been signed into force as a treaty. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>The voters who turned out to oppose the &quot;constitution&quot; felt uncomfortable about handing over sovereignty to Brussels. But it will happen anyway.</p>\u000A\u000A<blockquote><p>The treaty is a slimmed-down version of the European constitution, with a more modest name and without any reference to EU symbols such as the flag and anthem.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>\u000A\u000AIt is meant to ease decision-making, by scrapping national vetoes in some 50 policy areas, including sensitive ones such as police and judicial co-operation. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>There will also be a foreign policy chief, controlling a big budget and thousands of diplomats and officials, and a permanent EU president appointed for up to five years.&nbsp; </p></blockquote><p>&quot;Ease decision making&quot; huh. What that really&nbsp; means is that if the people in a place like Slovakia (say) don't like what the gnomes in Brussels have decided for them tough cookies.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Ironically the actual signing of the treaty which will become known as the Treaty of Lisbon highlights some of the absurdities of EU&nbsp; politics.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Under the Treaty of Nice (2000) all&nbsp; summits of EU leaders must take place in Brussels.&nbsp; Thus after congregating in Lisbon for yesterday's formal signing (Portugal currently holds the rotating EU presidency)&nbsp; all the EU leaders and their foreign ministers decamped and flew to Brussels for the&nbsp; summit scheduled for today. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Which all seems rather hypocritical in these days of angst over mankind's carbon footprint.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Though to be fair the Prime ministers of Belgium, the Netherlands and\u000ALuxembourg did plane-pool as a gesture of social responsibility.</p></div>

This money is public&nbsp;property.</p>\u000A<p>Winston Peters has given the $158,000 due the taxpayer to a charity of his choosing. If any other taxpayer did this the Inland Revenue would pursue him for the&nbsp;debt.</p>\u000A<p>Mr Peters has not technically broken the law but only because he has used his party's votes in Parliament to help legalise the spending at the last election that the Auditor-General believes to be wrong. He has always disagreed with the Auditor-General's ruling and had wanted to contest it in the courts. But he has dropped this action, he says, because he could not have gotten a decision before the election next year and did not want to face the election accused of refusing to pay back "stolen&nbsp;money".</p>\u000A<p>So he has given it to the Starship. By accepting a donation that properly belongs to the public revenue it is complicit in an act of political manipulation and potentially depriving parts of the health service that may be less well endowed of&nbsp;funds.</p>\u000A<p>If the hospital means to keep this money it is obliged to explain to taxpayers why it believes the <span class="caps">NZ</span> First Party was entitled to dispose of the misspent election funds as it wished. This is not a political-legal dispute a public hospital would be wise to enter. The Starship would be well advised to return the cheque or, even better, pay it into the public accounts where it&nbsp;belongs.</p>\u000A<p>As for Mr Peters, the public doesn't seem surprised. Stunts of transparent nonsense have long been his preferred mode of operation. Most people have ceased to take him too seriously. VIdeology and education
p344

Vhttp://newzealandconservative.blogspot.com/2007/12/ideology-and-education.html

VAs someone who believes that too many people go to university these days, I was mildly pleased to hear that the University of Auckland is planning to restrict entry to all undergraduate courses for 2009 ("<a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/metro/story.cfm?l_id=117&amp;objectid=10480136">University Senate back plan on numbers</a>," <em>New Zealand Herald</em> Dec 4, 2007).<br /><br />The university says it is making the changes to cope with a shortfall of money driven by cut backs in central government funding. Hence the university is planning to limit entry for art, education, science, theology and first year law. Not sure about the science limits, but the other cut backs sound excellent.<br /><br />Over the last twenty years, the value of a university degree has steadily declined, as more and more marginal students, who have neither the academic aptitude or the intellectual curiosity for university level courses, have drifted through the system to satisfy the government\u2019s crude targets for more "human capital" throughput.<br /><br />Unfortunately, as I read on, I realised that my initial impression, that for once common sense might trump ideology, was too good to be true.Predictably, the University deputy vice-Chancellor, Professor Raewyn Dalziel, says the institution plans to establish a taskforce to increase enrolment of under-represented students:<br /><br /><em>"The special admission schemes which set aside places for Maori, Pacific, and other under-represented communities operating in facilities which already restrict entry will be expanded."<br /><br /></em>If, by "under represented communities," the University means students from low-income families, then this looks to be another kick in the face for hard-working students and parents from lower-middle class families who tend to suffer the most from affirmative action policies.<br /><br />While low-income families receive generous government allowances, and upper middle class kids can usually rely on parental support, students from middle-income families are caught in the middle - too well-off to be eligible receive allowances, yet not rich enough to be able to rely on significant help from their parents. Now their opportunities to cover the cost of their courses, through scholarships or other subsidies, are likely to be further limited.<br /><br />As I\u2019ve said before, only indigenous minorities have a reasonable case for preferential treatment, and even then, they should have to accept cutbacks in quotas when others are having to make sacrifices.

VTarget Practice
p353
sg6
Vhttp://blog.greens.org.nz/index.php/2007/12/14/target-practice/
p354
sg8
(lp355
sg10
V<p>Well, it looks like the US, China, Canada and Japan are going to hold Bali to ransom and prevent anything substantial from coming out of it. Not that I expected any grand outcome, just a decent framework to keep the post-Kyoto negotiations going. A couple of weeks ago, I posted a link to <a href="http://www.carbonequity.info/PDFs/Arctic.pdf" target="_blank">The Big Melt, Lessons from the Arctic Summer of 2007</a>. The folks over at <a href="http://www.carbonequity.info/index.html" target="_blank">CarbonEquity</a> had already published a sequel, <a href="http://www.carbonequity.info/PDFs/targets.pdf" target="_blank">Target Practice</a>, which talks about the way we are setting our climate change targets and whether or not it makes sense to do it that way. They offer a couple of alternative possibilities.</p>\u000A<p>One such alternative is that if a complete melt of the Arctic Sea ice over summer, which has no effect on sea levels, could trigger a collapse of the Greenland ice sheet which <em>could</em> affect sea levels, maybe one target would be to keep the chance of a complete Arctic melt down to one in a million. NASA decided in the sixties that keeping the odds of a Saturn rocket crashing into population centres at 1 to 1 million was about right. Why not apply the same odds to our climate change debate? This eliminates the politics and injects a definable, science based outcome.</p>\u000A<p>So if we agree that losing Greenland's ice sheet is bad because it means 5 - 10 metres or so of sea level rise, and losing the Arctic Sea ice will likely trigger this, how about we keep the odds of a complete Arctic Sea meltdown at 1 to 1 million? Here's how we've been doing since 1979 and where we're headed now:</p>\u000A<p>\u000A\u000A</p>\u000A<p>If you have a moment, follow the link to <a href="http://www.carbonequity.info/PDFs/targets.pdf" target="_blank">Target Practice</a>. It's much more upbeat than <a href="http://www.carbonequity.info/PDFs/Arctic.pdf" target="_blank">The Big Melt.</a></p>
p356

VANZ campaign goes international
p362
sg6
Vhttp://blog.greens.org.nz/index.php/2007/12/14/anz-campaign-goes-international/
p363
sg8
(lp364
sg10
V<p>The campaign against ANZ for providing finance to Rimbunan Hijau in PNG, to enable RH to carry out illegal and unsustainable logging, has linked up with the campaign against ANZ as the potential financier to the Gunns pulp mill in Tasmania. We had protests in NZ while the greens in Oz had similar protests earlier this week. The Sydney Morning Herald had a good <a href="http://news.smh.com.au/greenies-rally-against-anz-over-logging/20071212-1goa.html">article </a>on it.</p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<h3>Greenies rally against ANZ over logging</h3>\u000A<ul>\u000A<li class="adSpot-toolbox">\u000A<h3>December 12, 2007 - 8:12PM</h3>\u000A</li>\u000A</ul>\u000A<p><!--articleDetails--></p>\u000A<p class="articleExtras-wrap"><!-- adSpotIsland --></p>\u000A<p id="adSpotIsland" class="islandad">Environmentalists staged protests outside ANZ Bank branches in Australia and New Zealand calling on the bank not to fund logging operations in Tasmania and Papua New Guinea.</p>\u000A<p>The Wilderness Society of Tasmania and New Zealand's Green Party organised the protests to coincide with the United Nations climate change conference in Bali, Indonesia.</p>\u000A<p>Wilderness Society spokesman Paul Oosting said logging and land-clearing in Tasmania already accounted for at least 30 per cent of the state's greenhouse gas emissions and a proposed new pulp mill was conservatively estimated to add two per cent to Australia's annual emissions.</p>\u000A<p>"Both governments and banks have a global responsibility to help cut greenhouse gas emissions," he said.</p>\u000A<p>"This starts with refusing support for destructive logging practices and moving to help protect intact native forests."</p>\u000A<p>In New Zealand, Green Party co-leader Russel Norman called on customers to pressure the ANZ banking group, which has been named as a potential financier of the proposed pulp mill, not to "provide finance for forest destruction" in the state.</p>\u000A<p>Oosting said Tasmanian forests were some of the most "carbon rich" in the world and ancient trees 70-80 metres tall were being felled in the state's Styx Valley, in a woodchip-driven logging operation.</p>\u000A<p>He said the proposed new pulp mill would consume up to 4.5 million tonnes of wood a year, creating greenhouse gases equivalent to putting an extra 2.3 million cars on the road annually.</p>\u000A<p>Oosting said the Malaysian company Rimbunan Hijau, an ANZ client, was carrying out logging in Papua New Guinea that had been condemned internationally.</p>\u000A<p>Australian Greens leader Bob Brown said: "ANZ has a fantastic opportunity to behave as a good corporate citizen. It must take a strong stance against bankrolling the disastrous proposed Tasmanian mill and refuse to support the unsustainable and illegal logging of rainforests in Papua New Guinea."</p></blockquote>\u000A<p><!-- Copyright Sign --></p>

VMelchester Rovers \u2013 playing and trading fair
p369
sg6
Vhttp://blog.greens.org.nz/index.php/2007/12/14/melchester-rovers-%e2%80%93-playing-and-trading-fair/
p370
sg8
(lp371
sg10
V<p>Dunedin football team, the Melchester Rovers is the first team on this side of the world to exclusively use fair trade footballs for training and match play. Dave Peck, the promoter of fair trade sports balls and a Green Party member, plays in goal for Melchester and was interested to discover that fair trade balls cost the same to supply as traditional balls, except for the profit going to the communities that make them rather than the sports stars who promote them.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/melchester-photo-jul-07.jpg" alt="Melchester Rovers 07" /></p>\u000A<p>The production of soccer balls has long suffered from the abusive use of child labour in sweatshops.  Children are used by many of the factories that manufacture balls as cheaper, have small hands and eyesight that has not been ruined by stitching.</p>\u000A<p>Peck, the Rovers' British import, says he was given the task of replacing a ball that got lost in the harbour - not an issue that Cristiano Ronaldo faces but common enough in Dunedin.</p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<p>\u201CI searched for a local supplier of fair trade balls and after not finding one locally, I then discovered a supplier in Australia, to whom I contacted to order some training balls. A conversation eschewed and at the end of it I'd started importing them, with a shipment of a hundred balls heading over!\u201D</p>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p>According to <a href="http://www.etiko.co.nz/">Etiko</a>, the supplier of the balls, several challenges were posed when developing fair trade balls:</p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<p>\u201CInitially child labour had to be stopped while preventing children from seeking work in other areas.  Another challenge was to maintain the right of women to work.  In strict Islamic society football stitching is one of the few jobs readily available to women, as it can be done from home...</p>\u000A<p>The answer to the problem of child labour is surprisingly simple: pay workers properly! If parents of several children are forced to work for for wages that are so low they cannot support their families, then clearly children will be encouraged to work to bolster the family income... no parent would make their child work if they did not have to.\u201D</p>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p align="center"><img src="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/beckham-flyer-etiko-aug-07.jpg" alt="Etiko Beckham Flyer" /></p>

VClimate change: time to stop indulging the US
p376
sg6
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2007/12/climate-change-time-to-stop-indulging.html
p377
sg8
(lp378
sg10
V<p>Negotiators are Currently meeting at the United Nations Climate Change Conference in Bali in an effort to establish the framework for a successor to the Kyoto Protocol.  But as with previous talks on the subject, we're seeing the usual games, with the US (aided and abetted by its reliable stooges Canada and Japan) <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/2/story.cfm?c_id=2&objectid=10482316">attempting to disrupt the talks</a> and prevent them from agreeing to a ballpark target for future emissions reductions by developed nations of 25 - 40%.  They're also objecting to a statementthat emissions must peak and decline within a decade.  Both positions are mainstream scientific opinion, endorsed by the IPCC in its latest report, which makes a mockery of the US's claim to want "science driven" policy.\u000A\u000A<p>The US does this at every meeting.  They play no constructive role in negotiations, but attempt to wreck them and prevent others from reaching any positive agreement.  It's time we stopped indulging them, or pandering to their belief in their own relevance.  The US is run by a lame-duck President leading a lame-duck administration, and everyone knows policy will change when he leaves office in January 2009.  If the current US administration will not participate meaningfully in these negotiations, then the rest of the world should simply work around them, reach a strong agreement, and let Bush's successor join up when they enter office.

VKnols Project: Google Experimenting With User Generated Encyclopedic Pages
p567
sg6
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/200065292/knol_project_google_experiment.php
p568
sg8
(lp569
sg10
V<p><font>\u000A</font>The official <a href="http://googleblog.blogspot.com/2007/12/encouraging-people-to-contribute.html">Google blog</a> has a post tonight about a new project that's in closed, private beta.  The program is called Knols, or "units of knowledge."  Knols participants will write reference pages on any topic, using a Google content creation tool apparently in the works, and those pages will be highlighted in Google search results.  Authors will choose whether they want ads to appear and will receive a "substantial revenue share."\u000A</p><p>I think this is going to be a game changer.  Check out this sample page below.</p><p><center><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/thumb.png" /></center></p><p>\u000ACompeting Knols pages on the same topic will be judged by reader votes and the Google Search Quality process.  There will be reader commenting, the ability to add additional information and more social features.  It won't be a walled garden but will live on the open web.  Attribution will be substantial and Google is presumably working with high-profile topic specialists on the Knol project.\u000A</p>\u000A\u000A<p>\u000ASomewhere Jason Calacanis, his soul icy as it is, is aglow knowing that his <a href="http://mahalo.com">Mahalo</a> concept has been validated by a company that's arguably the most important in the last 100 years.  Likewise, there's probably some melancholy toasts due at <a href="http://squidoo.com">Squidoo</a> headquarters.  Those companies may or may not survive but the real battle will probably be with Wikipedia.  Google-built pages may be the only pages that have a bigger advantage in search than the widely linked Wikipedia reference pages.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=DflMnd"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=DflMnd" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=dAUQYHC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=dAUQYHC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=b50M3uC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=b50M3uC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=o6GuFVc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=o6GuFVc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=9WTT4Qc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=9WTT4Qc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=wlVy4nc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=wlVy4nc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=HNNu0WC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=HNNu0WC" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/200065292" height="1" width="1" />

VOmnidrive Heading for Deadpool?
p576
sg6
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/200020894/omnidrive_heading_for_deadpool.php
p577
sg8
(lp578
sg10
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/omnidrive_logo.gif" vspace="5" hspace="5" align="left" />A tipster informed us today that online storage solution <a href="http://www.omnidrive.com/">Omnidrive</a> has been having technical difficulties; and that the CTO has just left the company. Omnidrive's forums, both <a href="http://forum.omnidrive.com/topic/370#post-1740">the official one</a> and <a href="http://www.tangler.com/group/omnidrive-talk">the Tangler one</a>, are filled with messages complaining that the service is up and down - messages which the company doesn't appear to be responding to. The <a href="http://www.omnidrive.com/blog/2007/08/31/all-technical-difficulties-have-been-resolved/">last post</a> on the company's blog is dated August 31st and is entitled 'All technical difficulties have been resolved!'. There's also no recent postings on CEO <a href="http://www.nik.com.au/">Nik Cubrilovic's blog</a>.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/windows_live_skydrive_launched_online_storage.php">As we wrote in August</a>, the online storage space is very crowded - and there are a few monster players in the form of Microsoft, Google and Amazon. But Omnidrive was doing some great work in the space, <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/zoho_omnidrive_data_standards.php">driving for open standards</a> and partnering with other Web Office companies like Zoho.</p>\u000A<p>We've put in an email to Nik to clarify. I know him personally and it would be very sad if Omnidrive fell into the deadpool, particularly given the recent 'deaths' of Blognation and edgeio - two other web 2.0 startup collapses. As of now we're not ready to call Omnidrive as in the deadpool, but there seem to be major issues with the site judging by the forums.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/omnidrive_forum.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=Ahb9FD"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=Ahb9FD" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=DJXsEfC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=DJXsEfC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=TCUpZ0C"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=TCUpZ0C" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=kQrph6c"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=kQrph6c" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=1FXOpac"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=1FXOpac" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=TT2yZgc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=TT2yZgc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=wOY2oWC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=wOY2oWC" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/200020894" height="1" width="1" />

VBest Web LittleCo of 2007: Twitter
p583
sg6
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/199946129/best_web_littleco_of_2007_twitter.php
p584
sg8
(lp585
sg10
V<p>Earlier this week we announced our <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/best_web_bigco_of_2007.php">Best BigCo of 2007</a>, Facebook. In this post we're announcing our pick for Best LittleCo. We're also asking for your nominations for Most Promising Web Company for 2008. These picks are something we do every year, this being the 4th year. <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/best_web_littleco_2006.php">Last year's Best LittleCo</a> was <strong>YouTube</strong>, with <strong>Sharpcast</strong> selected as Most Promising. <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/best_web_compan.php">In 2005</a><strong> 37Signals</strong> was Best LittleCo and <strong>Memeorandum</strong> (now Techmeme) and <strong>Digg</strong> were joint Most Promising. <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/best_web_20_com.php">In 2004</a> <strong>Ludicorp</strong>, creators of Flickr, was Best LittleCo and <strong>Feedburner</strong> was named Most Promising. </p>\u000A<p>As you can see, most of our picks have gone on to enjoy more widespread success - YouTube, Ludicorp, Feedburner have all been acquired; while 37Signals, Techmeme, Digg and Sharpcast have all ramped up and enjoyed success. So to 2007, a year in which trends such as Mobile Web, social networking and micro-blogging have increased in popularity. It's been another bumper year of startup activity, so which among the hundreds of startups has impressed the most in 2007?</p>\u000A<h2>And the Winner is...</h2>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/twitter_logo.png" vspace="5" hspace="5" align="right" />As with the BigCo selection, the Read/WriteWeb authors were unanimous in our decision. <strong>The Best LittleCo of 2007 is <a href="http://twitter.com/help/aboutus">Twitter, Inc</a>.</strong> Already this week there has been a lot of analysis about <a href="http://www.twitter.com">Twitter</a>, with some people <a href="http://www.bubblegeneration.com/2007/12/whats-interesting-about-twitter-isnt.cfm">embracing</a> it and others <a href="http://publishing2.com/2007/12/11/why-i-stopped-using-twitter/">critical</a>. Our own Alex Iskold summed it up well in his post entitled <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/the_evolution_of_personal_publ.php">The Evolution of Personal Publishing</a>, when he described Twitter as a kind of mix between social networks and chat. The term for this has come to be know as <em>microblogging</em>. Here is how Alex described it:</p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A  <p>&quot;Social network publishing is very terse, blog publishing is verbose. Is there a form of publishing which is on one hand as easy as social networking, but as sequential as regular blogs? Twitter and Tumblr have recently emerged to define this new category of microblogging.&quot;</p>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/twitterlogo2.jpg" align="left" hspace="5px" vspace="5px" />The simple idea of Twitter is to express what you are doing right now, in 140 characters or less. Admittedly Twitter is still very much a niche, geek activity. Earlier this year I witnessed a fellow Web 2.0 Expo attendee twittering on a mobile phone while walking down a busy San Francisco road with a group of us - and she tripped up and fell. Which kind of sums up Twitter for the early adopter, geek crowd: it is addictive, distracting, and not really necessary. </p>\u000A<p>However RWW did highlight some real-world uses this year - e.g. <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/amazon_comes_to_twitter.php">Amazon uses it</a> to promote its products; and <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/lone_remaining_burmese_blogger.php">Burmese bloggers used a similar product</a> to Twitter, a lightweight messaging service called CBox, to post very short updates from inside the country. </p>\u000A<p>Twitter is undoubtedly <strong>new and disruptive</strong>. In a year in which you can count on one hand the number of disruptive Web products (iPhone would be another), Twitter stands out as being something that has captured the imagination and become a new hybrid of chat, social networking and blogging. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>One of the most important things Twitter has done is open up an API to outside developers (this is an argument that co-founder Biz Stone <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/twitter_open_platform_advantage.php">made to us</a> in September).  According to Twitter, the API has seen such incredible growth, that just months after it was released it is already getting 10 times the traffic of the Twitter web site. For examples, check out our <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/top_10_twitter_apps.php">Top 10 Twitter Apps</a> from July; and Marshall Kirkpatrick's comprehensive <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/the_rww_guide_to_the_worlds_mo.php">RWW Guide to the World's Most Popular Twitter Clients</a>.</p>\u000A<p>One of Twitter's cheif rivals, <a href="http://www.jaiku.com/">Jaiku</a>, was <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/google_acquires_jaiku.php">acquired by Google</a> in October. Other similar products that impressed us this year included (but not limited to): Tumblr, <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/kyte_its_like_t_1.php">Kyte</a> (a video twitter), <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/soup_tumble_blogging_with_friends.php">Soup</a>, <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/pownce_send_stuff_to_friends.php">Pownce</a>, and the <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/10_micro-blogging_tools_compared.php">10 microblogging tools</a> we reviewed in September.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/content-pipe.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p>See Also: <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/evolution_of_communication.php">Evolution of Communication: From Email to Twitter and Beyond</a></p>\u000A<h2>Nominations? Most Promising Web Company for 2008</h2>\u000A<p>So there you have it, Twitter is our Best LittleCo this year. Now we turn our attention to what is the most promising Web product or company for 2008 - and we need your help! Let us know in the comments what is most promising for you, and why. VFlickr Introduces Traffic Stats for Pro Users
p590
sg6
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/199878931/flickr_introduces_traffic_stats.php
p591
sg8
(lp592
sg10
V<p><font>\u000A</font><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/flickr_jan07.jpg" align="left" hspace="5px" vspace="5px" />Users with a pro account at <a href="http://flickr.com">Flickr</a> are now able to view a variety of interesting statistics about the viewers of their photos.  Heather Champ said in a post on the <a href="http://blog.flickr.com/en/2007/12/13/stats-stats-baby/">Flickr blog</a> this morning that the stats are intended to "give you all sorts of insight into how people arrive at your photos."\u000A</p><p>\u000AViewer numbers are a big deal for many Flickr users and Champ says this is one of their most requested features.  <strong>In a world increasingly full of user generated content platforms, offering users basic traffic stats like referring URLs ought to be standard practice.</strong> Offering these numbers to premium subscribers makes a lot of sense.  I expect this will be one more practice that Flickr blazes the trail on, only to be followed by others in a wide variety of markets.</p>\u000A<p>The stats feature needs to be activated by the user.  Large screenshots of the process can be found on <a href="http://blog.extraface.com/2007/12/13/flickr-stats-new-flickr-feature-on-the-way/">the blog of consultant Dave Coustan</a>, where I learned about the news myself.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=B2By1Z"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=B2By1Z" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=T90GeAC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=T90GeAC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=ob6mPhC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=ob6mPhC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=xyEDJ9c"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=xyEDJ9c" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=7ee0yQc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=7ee0yQc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=u80uXCc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=u80uXCc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=D5PLoZC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=D5PLoZC" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/199878931" height="1" width="1" />

VMobile MySpace On Sprint: Do Carrier Deals Make Sense?
p597
sg6
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/199862810/mobile_myspace_on_sprint_do_ca.php
p598
sg8
(lp599
sg10
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/myspace-logo.jpg" align="right" hspace="5px" vspace="5px" />Fox Interactive announced today that it has a deal with Sprint to offer one-click access to the new MySpace Mobile portal when it launches early next year.  Sprint and Fox have had a mobile relationship since before mobile meant much, in fact.  This could be a sneeze turned into a press release, but it's also a good opportunity to examine carrier-based mobile content deals vs. open social networking on mobile.</p>\u000A\u000A<p> <a href="http://money.cnn.com/news/newsfeeds/articles/djf500/200712130938DOWJONESDJONLINE000793_FORTUNE5.htm">Early press on the deal</a> says Sprint will be first but it does not say that it will be an exclusive deal.    It was around this same time last year that MySpace announced a deal with Cingular that would let that carrier's customers use a Java app for MySpace for $3 per month.  Helio, a high-profile handset that operates on the Sprint network, has allowed access to MySpace since last year as well.  This week Helio launched a mobile YouTube interface that <a href="http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/hr/content_display/business/news/e3icf7a9c3d15e7be1ce9172be6b3938e16">the company says</a> is the first to allow YouTube users access to their accounts and social features.\u000A</p><p>\u000A<strong>The primary question this raises, though, is this:</strong>  why not just open a free, universally accessible mobile MySpace like Facebook offers?  Facebook Mobile is excellent and would provide as good a model for MySpace as the Facebook Newsfeed did for the new MySpace friend feed.  (See our coverage of <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/social_networks_study_fabernovel.php">MySpace vs. Facebook in general</a>.) Just add some adds and superfluous pageviews and you've got MySpace Mobile. Perhaps MySpace felt it was not capable of monetizing mobile access except through carrier deals.  That would be interesting news for the rest of the industry.\u000A</p><p>\u000AMobile access could be a key step in MySpace regaining growth momentum, but that seems more likely if the company were to open mobile access to all.  It's an interesting trade-off and I wish I was a fly on the wall at the meetings where these decisions were being made.\u000A</p><h2>Tracking the Mobile Content World</h2><p>\u000AThanks to Forrester's <a href="http://web-stragist.com">Jeremiah Owyang</a>, who called attention to the news first in my world, on <a href="http://twitter.com/jowyang">Twitter</a>.  We're looking to increase our coverage of mobile news and issues here at ReadWriteWeb.  If you're interested in this space as well, you can download an OPML file (a bundle of RSS feeds for importing into your feed reader) that contains some of my favorite mobile content sources and mobile news from our blogs ReadWriteWeb and <a href="http://last100.com">Last100</a>, filtered via <a href="http://feedrinse.com">FeedRinse</a>: <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/files/rwwmobilefeeds.opml">RWWMobileFeeds.opml</a>.  Save the file behind that link, import it into your feed reader and you'll be up to date on the fast emerging world of mobile content.  You can preview the live contents of this collection below, using <a href="http://grazr.com">Grazr</a>.</p><p><center><div><a href="http://grazr.com/gzpanel.html?file=http://grazr.com/opml/marshallrww" target="gz"><img src="http://grazr.com/images/grazrbadge.png" border="0" /></a></div></center></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=I2SKhw"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=I2SKhw" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=9h29B1C"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=9h29B1C" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=QGrkrnC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=QGrkrnC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=vW7mrnc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=vW7mrnc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=Y1DKxAc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=Y1DKxAc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=cnwqpEc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=cnwqpEc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=69V1XPC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=69V1XPC" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/199862810" height="1" width="1" />

VGoogle and accounting\u2026
p604
sg6
Vhttp://diversity.net.nz/google-and-accounting/2007/12/14/
p605
sg8
(lp606
sg10
V<p>With a hat tip to a clean shaven Mike, this <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/online_accounting_google_apps.php" target="_blank">post</a> over on RWW surmises that an online accounting system might be in the pipline from Google. The rationale for the idea of Google entering this space is pretty much the rationale for them entering every space - eyeballs, data and stickiness.</p>\u000A<p>If we look however at who Google are - they are predominantly a mass market player - as such they're keen to get the maximum number of eyeballs in any one particular space.</p>\u000A<p>With that in mind, I'm picking that Google will launch a financial offering, but it'll be more along the lines of "Google your money" than "Google business money". I'm picturing home budgeting (obvious advertising fit there ) and cashflow. Some nice calculators to work stuff out and the like. All these things can be rolled out pretty globally without customisation, accounting is much more location specific and not completely within the current Google model.</p>\u000A<p>I'm sure they do have people looking at the business accounting space but I don't see it happening in the near future... but then again I could be wrong. I wonder if <a href="http://www.xero.com" target="_blank">Xero</a> feel like commenting on the possibiilty?</p>

VMintshot Update
p643
sg6
Vhttp://www.nzrealitytv.com/2007/12/mintshot-update.html
p644
sg8
(lp645
sg10
VAs regular readers of this site will be aware I've had a lot of problems with <a href="http://www.mintshot.co.nz/">Mintshot</a> and have been in contact with them to try and resolve the issues.<br /><br />Turns out that when I said I was one of handful of people who had <a href="http://www.nzrealitytv.com/2007/12/mintshot-play-people-other-errors.html">problems with yesterday's results</a> on my Play The People bets, that I was <span>literally </span>one of a handful. According to Nick Dalton, one of the directors of Mintshot, you could count the number of people who had that precise problem on one hand.<br /><br /><a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_HZlxBZQcoGI/R08kP1x28oI/AAAAAAAABQQ/lt_0ljjVmfo/s320/mintshot+logo.gif"><img alt="" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_HZlxBZQcoGI/R08kP1x28oI/AAAAAAAABQQ/lt_0ljjVmfo/s320/mintshot+logo.gif" border="0" /></a><br /><br />Mintshot have been extremely helpful, (not to mention relieved that it hasn't happened again this morning) and are beavering away testing their system to try to identify where the problem might have occurred. I'm not sure we'll ever get to the bottom of it, but I feel satisfied that they're taking the problem seriously and are keen to hear what users have to say about the system. I look forward to the day when I won't feel compelled to take screenshots of every bet!<br /><br />Nick tells me that Mint Tick (the game where you click to reveal ticks or crosses with the highest score winning prizes) is proving very popular, and has increased traffic to the site. I confess I've given it a go, but so far I haven't got anywhere near the number of ticks I need to win a prize.<br /><br />Also in "inside" news from Mintshot, I heard that the blog is currently in test mode and will be up on their site soon. Users will be able to check in to find out what's happening with the site and voice their concerns with interactive comments on the blog. Nick tells me that it's their intention to improve the community feel of the site with more opportunities for members to vote on what's happening. He assures me that Mintshot takes customer feedback seriously, and I believe him.<br /><br />Nick says the team are working closely with users to eliminate any cheats or shortcuts in the system that enable people to watch advertisements multiple times or find other ways to boost their points. Mintshot get daily reports of suspicious activity and act on it. That will be a relief to many, who are casting their eyes in suspicion at people who appear to have large mint dollar balances, have won lots of prizes or are doing well in the mint tick games. It's creating an atmosphere of distrust, as players accuse others of cheating and dob them in to Mintshot.<br /><br />After past problems with cheating, there is still a concern from some users that people are finding ways to cheat. If they are, I haven't heard about it, although I do know a lot of people took advantage of the problems that occurred in Monday's changeover of advertisements that enabled some people to watch advertisements multiple times. One user reported that they took advantage of the loophole and then got banned. He thought that was unfair.<br /><br />It's hard to know what's fair. On the one hand, some people wrote to Mintshot and pointed out the problem. For example, I emailed when I found that a McDonald's advertisement that I had already watched, could be watched a second time after the question changed, giving me an extra 200 mint dollars. Others say that if the system has problems, then it's fair game and they're entitled to take advantage of it. I can see both perspectives but personally I don't think it's worth it.<br /><br />Fingers crossed, this is the end of my hassles with Mintshot, and things go smoothly from now on. If not, you'll definitely be hearing from me...\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/NewZealandRealityTv?a=6y3Apf"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/NewZealandRealityTv?i=6y3Apf" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=GO5H1zC"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=GO5H1zC" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=LhvYLZc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=LhvYLZc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=ieTQRhc"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=ieTQRhc" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=6jXWZ3c"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=6jXWZ3c" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/NewZealandRealityTv/~4/199573753" height="1" width="1" />

V1 easy service to keep a track of EVERYTHING
p675
sg6
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MiramarMikesBlog/~3/199920301/1-easy-service-to-keep-track-of.html
p676
sg8
(lp677
sg10
VMost of my online friends (that happily are becoming actual friends) rarely limit themselves to one online presence for a many reasons - one service rarely does it all, you need to <a href="http://miramarmike.blogspot.com/2007/11/5-easy-ways-to-protect-your-online.html">protect your online presence from ID theft</a> and we are generally early adopters and try a gazillion services before settling on one.<br /><br />I'll use myself as an example - you can find me actively online at:<br /><ul><li>this blog</li><li>Flickr for my photos</li><li>delicious for my bookmarks</li><li>YouTube for uploaded videos</li><li>Wellingtonista for my Wellington blogging</li><li>Facebook for my "this is me status"</li></ul>And that's just the day-to-day active ones - <a href="http://miramarmike.blogspot.com/2006/12/about-miramarmike.html">I'm 'at' a lot more places</a>.<br /><br />Whilst I've <a href="http://miramarmike.blogspot.com/2007/04/miramarmike-rss-feed-now-supports-all.html">set-up a few RSS feeds</a> for some of the more useful ones wouldn't it be grand just to subscribe to one feed and it all comes through? And that's the same for nearly everyone I know.<br /><br /><div><a href="http://friendfeed.com/" title="FriendFeed"><img src="http://i6.photobucket.com/albums/y211/miramarmike/logo-1.png" alt="FriendFeed" border="0" /></a><br /></div>FriendFeed is such a service that I have been running with for a month or so.<br />After you sign-up* it is extremely easy to click and add the services you use - click to add your delicious bookmarks feed, click and you've added your Flickr photo feed ...<br /><br />And then it's one feed to give to people - mine is <a href="http://friendfeed.com/miramarmike?format=atom">http://friendfeed.com/miramarmike?format=atom</a> - and have everything fed through.<br />No more having to worry about letting your friends know, "Oh, I've just started using X for tracking my movie going adventures and I think you'd love to know when I've seen a film"<br /><br />FriendFeed feeds out using:<br /><ul><li><a href="http://friendfeed.com/miramarmike?format=atom">Into your feed reader</a></li><li><a href="http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=654055951">Facebook app</a></li><li><a href="http://friendfeed.com/embed?user=miramarmike">Embed into a website</a></li><li><a href="http://www.google.com/ig/add?url=http://friendfeed.com/embed/googlegadget/spec">iGoogle</a><br /></li></ul><br />Aaaaand, you can manage who is using FriendFeed to subscribe to you ... if you want.<br /><br /><span>* I know, you do have to sign-up - I can't wait for the growing adoption of OpenID</span><div class="blogger-post-footer"><hr />\u000A<small>\u000A<a href="http://miramarmike.blogspot.com/search/label/enterprise%202.0" title="Subscribe to MirmarMike's Enterprise 2.0 postings">Enterprise 2.0 New Zealand style</a> since 2001<br />\u000A<a href="http://miramarmike.blogspot.com/2007/04/miramarmike-rss-feed-now-supports-all.html" title="Subscribe to MiramarMike">Subscribe to other parts of MiramarMike</a> (Wellington, New Zealand)<br />\u000A</small></div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MiramarMikesBlog/~4/199920301" height="1" width="1" />

V<div class="snap_preview"><p>I've now got the sort of job that's going to require me to be in a situation where free alcoholic beverages are readily on hand and it would be almost rude of me not to partake. In several. Several too many.</p>\u000A<p>My new office is also located in an area that is dangerously close to many of the city's less reputable entertainment establishments. VNational reopens Selwyn nominations
p806
sg6
Vhttp://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2007/12/national_reopens_selwyn_nominations.html
p807
sg8
(lp808
sg10
V<p>National announced last night that it has decided to reopen nominations for Selwyn, after <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/thepress/4323181a19720.html">complaints of pressure</a> on some candidates not to stand.</p>\u000A<p>This is not a common occurrence.  I don't think I can recall another selection where this has happened.</p>\u000A<p>I know absolutely nothing about the details, beyond what I have read in the newspaper.   But what I can say is what my personal view is.</p>\u000A<p>I think every seat not currently held by National should have an active selection contest.  Yes it can be challenging for managing parliamentary relationships, but overall the party gains members and supporters when we have contested selections for seats National does not hold.</p>\u000A<p>Another reason I support contested selections, is that on current polling National could gain 55 - 60 MPs.  And with a policy that all but a maximum of five list candidates must also be electorate candidates, it means that even candidates in the most safe Labour seats have a significant chance of becoming MPs through the list.  And a healthy selection process can help ensure that National doesn't end up with "dud" MPs as happened in 1990.</p>\u000A<p>National of course also has a history of selection battles for sitting electorate MPs - John Key, Judith Collins and John Carter all won their seats by challenging for the nomination against an incumbent electorate MP.  And National is far better off for having had them do so.</p>\u000A<p>The issue of List MPs is a bit different.  A List MP doesn't hold a seat, even though they may have stood for it last time or be associated with it.  There isn't the same stigma to stand against a List MP for a seat, as there is to actually challenge an Electorate MP.  For example Annabel Young faced a contested selection for Wellington Central despite being an existing List MP.</p>\u000A<p>So National has a good healthy history of contested selections, and it is good to see the same will happen in Selwyn - safe seats especially should have a vigorous contest.</p>

V<p>Some commenters on the left are always going on about the important of disclosure, and go into a fury if a Richard Long column (for example) doesn't appear with a disclaimer that he used to work for Don Brash (as indeed did I).</p>\u000A<p>And I noticed yesterday The Standard also finally managed to <a href="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=859#comment-9812">find a column</a> in a newspaper in favour of the Electoral Finance Bill.</p>\u000A<p>It is written by Simon Cunliffe, a senior ODT journalist.</p>\u000A<p>Strangely though, they did not think it necessary to mention that Mr Cunliffe was just two months ago a press secretary to a Labour Minister.</p>\u000A<p>Now I don't think this in anyway diminishes the legitimacy of Simon Cunliffe's opinion.  He has every right to write his honest opinion of the Electoral Finance Bill.</p>\u000A<p>I just thought there was a double standard for those insisting every Richard Long column mention his previous job (which now was over two years ago) and not applying the same standard to someone who had a political role much more recently.</p>

VNZ First on Electoral Reform
p820
sg6
Vhttp://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2007/12/nz_first_on_electoral_reform.html
p821
sg8
(lp822
sg10
V<p>A commenter yesterday pointed out a clause in <a href="http://www.nzfirst.org.nz/principles/index.php">NZ First's 15 fundamental principles</a>, which highlights their hypocrisy on the Electoral Finance Bill:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><em><strong>Electoral Reform</strong></em></p>\u000A<p><em>Electoral reform will be determined by the electors. The Government's duty will be to ensure the fair representation of all views and the holding of appropriate referenda. </em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>So consider this:</p>\u000A<ol>\u000A<li>The public had no notice before the last election of electoral law changes</li>\u000A<li>NZ First negotiated in secret with Labour on electoral law changes</li>\u000A<li>There was no public policy process to allow policy to be set on which the law was based</li>\u000A<li>Opinion polls (Colmar Brunton) have shown the majority against further third party restrictions</li>\u000A<li>The Human Rights Commission called for a second round of public submissions, which NZ First ignored</li>\u000A<li>The public will be restrained from criticising those who voted for the law, by the law.</li>\u000A</ol>\u000A<p>So is that what NZ First calls having electoral reform determined by the electors?</p>

VHerald calls on Starship to give the money back
p827
sg6
Vhttp://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2007/12/herald_calls_on_starship_to_give_the_money_back.html
p828
sg8
(lp829
sg10
V<p>Winston's stunt may be backfiring. The <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/story.cfm?c_id=280&amp;objectid=10482229">Herald editorial</a> is blunt:</p>\u000A<p>The Starship children's hospital should immediately return the cheque it has received from the New Zealand First Party. This money is public property.</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><em>Mr Peters has not technically broken the law but only because he has used his party's votes in Parliament to help legalise the spending at the last election that the Auditor-General believes to be wrong. He has always disagreed with the Auditor-General's ruling and had wanted to contest it in the courts. But he has dropped this action, he says, because he could not have gotten a decision before the election next year and did not want to face the election accused of refusing to pay back "stolen money".</em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>This claim that they could not have got a hearing in time is one media should treat with suspicion.  The Auditor-General ruled in the latter half of 2006.  I have not seen anything to suggest that one could not have got a court hearing within two years.  For example the lawsuit against the Electoral Finance Bill only has a six month wait for a hearing.</p>\u000A<p>The other point to remember is that there was a lawsuit which would have tested whether the Auditor-General was correct.  Darnton vs Clark.  With regards to the Labour pledge card at least, this would have resulted in a court ruling whether or not the expenditure was legal.</p>\u000A<p>NZ First voted to kill off the lawsuit, voting against an amendment that would have stopped the validating legislation retrospectively killing off the lawsuit.</p>
