VSlightly less super
p850
sg6
Vhttp://wellurban.blogspot.com/2007/12/slightly-less-super.html
p851
sg8
(lp852
sg10
V<div class="file-under">File under: <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/urbanism" rel="tag">urbanism</a>, <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/Mt+Cook" rel="tag">Mt Cook</a>, <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/Wellington" rel="tag">Wellington</a></div><br />When you're considering what to submit for <a href="http://wellurban.blogspot.com/2007/11/growing-spine.html">the Adelaide Rd consultation</a> (due in less than 4 hours), it's worth bearing in mind the current state of proposed private developments. There was an article in yesterday's <span>Dominion Post</span> (not online), and a <a href="http://wellington.govt.nz/news/display-item.php?id=3090">media release from the council</a>, stating that a demolition consent has been applied for for the proposed supermarket site that has been <a href="http://wellurban.blogspot.com/2007/08/mt-cook-summit.html">much discussed</a>. While both articles are primarily concerned about the possibility of the site being left vacant for months, there's a small point mentioned in the Dom article that's quite interesting: the proposal has been scaled down somewhat.<br /><br />Instead of a 6000 sq m <span>Pak 'N Save</span> with 60 apartments, <span>Foodstuffs</span> are now proposing "a medium-sized <span>New World</span> supermarket above a car park with space for 157 vehicles, and a couple of four to five-storey blocks, each with 20 apartments". The façade of <a href="http://mtcookmobilised.pbwiki.com/Preserving+heritage+values+-+the+BGI">the old BGI swimming pool</a> will also be retained and incorporated, and while I'm always wary of façadism, this all sounds like some sort of compromise is happening quietly during the pre-application stage of the consent process. If the actual consent process (which <span>Foodstuffs</span> expects to start in March) were able to ensure that the final design incorporates plenty of active edges and maybe even a replacement for the pool, then I think we could go a long way towards balancing the needs of what could be a valuable development with the legitimate concerns of current residents. Fingers crossed.

VFrank comparisons
p859
sg6
Vhttp://wellurban.blogspot.com/2007/12/frank-comparisons.html
p860
sg8
(lp861
sg10
V<div class="file-under">File under: <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/waterfront" rel="tag">waterfront</a>, <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/urbanism" rel="tag">urbanism</a>, <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/landscape+architecture" rel="tag">landscape architecture</a>, <a href="http://technorati.com/tag/Wellington" rel="tag">Wellington</a></div><br />The winner of the Frank Kitts Park design competition has been announced (on page A4 of today's <span>Dominion Post</span> and in <a href="http://www.wellingtonwaterfront.co.nz/media_section/Publications/on_the_waterfront/newsletters.htm?m=65">the latest issue of <span>On the Waterfront</span></a>), and it was the one labelled <a href="http://wellurban.blogspot.com/2007/10/frank-kitts-option-b.html">Option B</a>. As I speculated at the time but couldn't say for sure, it's by Wraight and Associates, who were part of the Waitangi Park design team. Interestingly, the announcement includes a perspective drawing that makes it much easier to grasp the overall layout than the entry itself did.<br /><br /><a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_Y5J8pfNiQA4/R2G31fVLcLI/AAAAAAAAAk4/ZOFUa4uhijw/s1600-h/frank_kitts_proposed_perspective.jpg"><img src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_Y5J8pfNiQA4/R2G31fVLcLI/AAAAAAAAAk4/ZOFUa4uhijw/s400/frank_kitts_proposed_perspective.jpg" border="0" alt="Winning design for Frank Kitts Park" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5143594379005096114" /></a>In my <a href="http://wellurban.blogspot.com/2007/11/last-chance-feedback.html">summary of the options</a>, I said of this one that it has "Nice clean geometry, with a good tight cluster of buildings, but too much bleakly flat lawn." I think I still stand by that, but that's partly based on my own personal aversion to big open paddocks, and people who want a big flat space for chucking around a ball or frisbee should be very pleased with this. In fact, for all the talk in some quarters of the redesign "destroying open space", it looks like this plan actually has more open green space than the current park:<br /><br /><a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_Y5J8pfNiQA4/R2GsMPVLcKI/AAAAAAAAAkw/tcVOK3NHVqc/s1600-h/frank_kitts_old_vs_proposed.jpg"><img src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_Y5J8pfNiQA4/R2GsMPVLcKI/AAAAAAAAAkw/tcVOK3NHVqc/s400/frank_kitts_old_vs_proposed.jpg" alt="Current Frank Kitts Park layout compared to selected new design" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5143581575707586722" border="0" /></a>The most important thing is to compare the new design to the current park. On the plus side, this will finally be a waterfront park from which you can actually see the water. It will be an opportunity to update the physical and design qualities of a park that is looking rather tired and dated. The Chinese Garden, which I think is handled better than in any of the rival designs, should provide a lot of spatial variety, visual interest, shelter and cultural value. The upper lawn will have better access from the promenade and lagoon, and in general movement into and through the park should be easier. Best of all, from my perspective, the cluster of pavilions in and adjacent to the Chinese Garden has the potential to create a node of activity part way along a stretch that can be quite deserted at times.<br /><br />Apart from the exposed nature of the lawn space, there are a few other aspects I'm less happy with. I don't see the need to relocate the Albatross sculpture to the upper lawn: it's very popular where it is, and the current combination of lagoon, fountain and <span>Kaffee Eis</span> works very well. The larger flat green area comes at the expense of the amphitheatre, so while it will be better for some sorts of events it will be less suited to others. There's no attempt to create new connections between the promenade and the water, though the brief suggested that this might be left until later stages for financial reasons. Finally, the improved visual connection between the lawn and the harbour comes at the expense of shelter and seating along the promenade: while the loss of shelter may be an unavoidable trade-off, I hope that some sort of informal or moveable seating could be included without too much effort.<br /><br />The article emphasised that this is not a final, detailed design, and that more development of the design will occur over the next six months. There's a lot to like about this proposal, and I hope that between now and the eventual reconstruction of the park (which is unlikely to start before 2009), there are opportunities to work through any shortcomings and create the best possible space.

VHerald Editorial says "Give it back"

V<p><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/466/story.cfm?c_id=466&amp;objectid=10482229" rel="nofollow">Editorial: Starship should give money back - 14 Dec 2007 - Opinion, Editorial and reader comments from New Zealand and around the World -&nbsp;nzherald</a></p>\u000A<p><div class="quote-msg"><div class="quote-author">Quote:</div>The Starship children's hospital should immediately return the cheque it has received from the New Zealand First Party. This money is public&nbsp;property.</p>\u000A<p>Winston Peters has given the $158,000 due the taxpayer to a charity of his choosing. If any other taxpayer did this the Inland Revenue would pursue him for the&nbsp;debt.</p>\u000A<p>Mr Peters has not technically broken the law but only because he has used his party's votes in Parliament to help legalise the spending at the last election that the Auditor-General believes to be wrong. He has always disagreed with the Auditor-General's ruling and had wanted to contest it in the courts. But he has dropped this action, he says, because he could not have gotten a decision before the election next year and did not want to face the election accused of refusing to pay back "stolen&nbsp;money".</p>\u000A<p>So he has given it to the Starship. It is extraordinary that the hospital has accepted the money in these circumstances. It perhaps has not given enough thought to the&nbsp;implications.</p>\u000A<p>Advertisement<br />&nbsp;Advertisement</p>\u000A<p>It is letting itself be used for a petty political purpose. Mr Peters is using public sympathy for sick children to avoid a payment he believes his party should not have to make. Rather than accept the ruling against him and return the money to the public purse he has put the amount in a place he calculates to be beyond public&nbsp;reproach.</p>\u000A<p>The Starship is being cynically used and must know it. The hospital is part of the public health service. By accepting a donation that properly belongs to the public revenue it is complicit in an act of political manipulation and potentially depriving parts of the health service that may be less well endowed of&nbsp;funds.</p>\u000A<p>If the hospital means to keep this money it is obliged to explain to taxpayers why it believes the <span class="caps">NZ</span> First Party was entitled to dispose of the misspent election funds as it wished. This is not a political-legal dispute a public hospital would be wise to enter. The Starship would be well advised to return the cheque or, even better, pay it into the public accounts where it&nbsp;belongs.</p>\u000A<p>As for Mr Peters, the public doesn't seem surprised. Stunts of transparent nonsense have long been his preferred mode of operation. Most people have ceased to take him too seriously. He is excused for impish behaviour that would not be accepted from anyone else in public&nbsp;office.</p>\u000A<p>Seldom, though, has he displayed such contempt for public opinion and public finance as he has on this occasion. He freely admitted yesterday that the misuse of party allowances at the 2005 election was an issue "on which the court of public opinion had already made its final&nbsp;ruling".</p>\u000A<p>Since his party could not get a contrary declaration from the courts before the end of next year, he said, it proceeded to raise the amount the Auditor-General ruled that it owed but it was not willing to see the money disappear into the Government coffers.</div></p>\u000A<p class="poweredbyperformancing">Powered by <a href="http://scribefire.com/" rel="nofollow">ScribeFire</a>.</p>

VMore on the PM\u2019s views on the media
p2989
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/politics/2007/12/14/more-on-the-pms-views-on-the-media/
p2990
sg8
(lp2991
sg10
V<p>Silence has descended over Parliament today. The MPs got through their urgency last night so there will be one final hurrah next Tuesday to hold the third reading of the Electoral Finance Bill, a final Question Time and perhaps one more first reading and then it's up stumps and off for Christmas.</p>\u000A<p>It's been an intriguing week, dominated by the oddest and smallest of stories - the Prime Minister's speech to the Journalism Education Association conference in Wellington. A few throwaway remarks by Helen Clark have got her into trouble with parts of the press gallery - notably the political editors of TV1 and TV3, Guyon Espiner and Duncan Garner.</p>\u000A<p>As is so often the case, it's not what the Prime Minister originally said but what has happened since that is so interesting. </p>\u000A<p>The Prime Minister, who values her relationship with the gallery and has always gone to some lengths to preserve it - now wants to move on. But I'd like a transcript, or better still, a tape of her address to the journalists. Her office has one, but it won't release it. </p>\u000A<p>I know what you're thinking - why wasn't I there? Well, just to get this clear, because the Prime Minister's office thinks this is important, <em>I didn't attend her speech</em>. There has been some comment that this is an important factor - even that it means I don't have the right to blog on the topic. For the record, I would have liked to go but a) I was at home in bed sick and b) I didn't know about it anyway.</p>\u000A<p>Only one press gallery reporter attended. No one has a tape. Most didn't know about the Prime Minister's appearance either. We have been criticised for this. The Prime Minister's office points out that the engagement was in the ministerial diary forwarded to the press gallery each week. That's true. But no advisory was sent out, which is unusual. Normally we are encouraged to attend her speeches, although obviously we can't always do so.</p>\u000A<p>Anyway, now that's clear, I am relying on what was reported by <em>New Zealand Herald</em> journalist Claire Trevett, who did attend, and wrote a story which to the best of my knowledge Clark has not taken issue with. So what follows is based on <a target="_blank" href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/category/story.cfm?c_id=49&amp;objectid=10481591"><strong>what Claire wrote </strong></a>and also speaking to others who were there. </p>\u000A<p>In her presentation to the conference, Clark said many journalists were young, and while this meant that they had "energy and a fresh perspective", most of them had major gaps in their general knowledge.</p>\u000A<p>Clark said "very few" journalists had a comprehensive knowledge of New Zealand's international relations and few media outlets sent journalists to cover her international trips.</p>\u000A<p>"It's a matter of regret that proprietors don't seem to think these things are particularly important either, so they don't encourage the depth of coverage."</p>\u000A<p>She also said media also needed to consider blogging by senior political reporters on the websites of major news outlets. </p>\u000A<p>"Of course, if you commit yourself to instant opinion, then when it comes time to putting in a considered piece, you might think, 'Whoops, that was a rush of judgment,' but it becomes hard to climb back from."</p>\u000A<p>Clark only mentioned one journalist by name, Duncan Garner, who she said was an example of a journalist too willing to confuse scutiny with cynicism, and who recently claimed that all politicians lied.</p>\u000A<p>Garner tells me this was a poor paraphrase of a remark he made recently to a journalism industry event, at which he said, referring to the Benson-Pope saga, that when cornered, a politician's first instinct was to lie.  </p>\u000A<p>I can think of a few MPs this applies to, although Clark has every right to say these things, and they are food for thought. Worthy of debate. I'm intrigued, then, as to why her office won't release the rest of what she said so I can post it here for everyone to read or listen to.</p>\u000A<p>One could draw the conclusion that it is because the Prime Minister realises she went too far in some of her remarks and unfairly denigrated some senior journalists. That she wants the issue closed, because attacking the Fourth Estate is never very productive for a politician. And perhaps, there is more on the tape she'd prefer didn't get reported.</p>\u000A<p>I could be completely wrong. I'm just saying one could come to that conclusion, given the PM's office's peculiar refusal to release the tape.</p>\u000A<p>As regular On the House readers will know, the PM's press secretary Juli Clausen posted an entry for the first time the other day, criticising me for not attending the speech and also making errors in my earlier post. I'm grateful for her post. According to her office the PM didn't actually use the words "too young to remember history", and if that's the case they should not have been in speech marks.</p>\u000A<p>I was unhappy about clarifying this without a transcript of what Clark actually said, which as I said has proven elusive. The PM's office has since dropped its request for a correction, but I've been trying to find out what she did say anyway.</p>\u000A<p>This little media storm in a teacup has been picked up by <em>Media Watch</em>, Radio New Zealand's weekly look at the media, which has interviewed both Clark and Garner. Amongst the remarks the PM makes on the programme are that news organisations don't appear willing to pay the salaries necessary to retain the sorts of senior journalists one would expect to be in high-ranking news jobs in New Zealand.</p>\u000A<p>But Clark denies this is the same thing as saying those who are doing the jobs in New Zealand are too young for their positions. </p>\u000A<p>To my knowledge it's the first time the PM has appeared on <em>Media Watch</em>, and it would be <a target="_blank" href="http://www.radionz.co.nz/nr/programmes/mediawatch"><strong>worth a listen </strong></a>(Sunday 9am and 10pm on RNZ and posted on their website).</p>

VEarly Christmas presents and Labour\u2019s pains
p2998
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/toonedin/2007/12/14/early-christmas-presents-and-labours-pains/
p2999
sg8
(lp3000
sg10
V<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/rickards4.jpg" title="rickards4.jpg"></a><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/rickards4-295-x-561.jpg" title="rickards4-295-x-561.jpg"></a><img vspace="5" width="265" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/rickards4-295-x-561.jpg" hspace="5" alt="rickards4-295-x-561.jpg" height="505" title="rickards4-295-x-561.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p>This will have to be a brief post since my wife is going into labour and I need to finish my cartoon for tomorrow as soon as possible. Yikes! No pressure, eh? Fortunately there's lots of good material to choose from.</p>\u000A<p>We're planning to have a home birth, so I'll be around the house throughout the day, popping in and out from my studio. We had our last child at home too, and I was working at the <em>Nelson Mail</em> at the time. I remember finishing at 11am as soon as the paper went to press, then racing home on my bike as Fran's contractions were getting stronger and more frequent. By 1:30pm we had a new addition to our family. Talk about good timing!</p>\u000A<p>Anyway, here are some new pics. VMake \u2018em sweat, Fabio
p3007
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/handofgod/2007/12/14/make-em-sweat-fabio/
p3008
sg8
(lp3009
sg10
V<p>Times could be about to get tougher for England's dismal band of underachieving footballers. If there's one thing <a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4323930a18075.html"><strong>Fabio Capello</strong> </a>believes in, it's the value of hard work. Just ask Ronaldo, Alessandro del Piero and Francesco Totti, who have all found themselves dropped by Capello for daring not to work hard enough.</p>\u000A<p>When Capello left Juventus, del Piero is reported to have said: "Now I can return to playing football with the love I have for it. The era of terror in training has now gone." Ruud van Nistelrooy said he has never worked as hard as he did under Capello at Real Madrid.</p>\u000A<p>The good news for England is that the common factor here is not the whining of highly paid prima donnas: it's that Juventus and Madrid - and Totti's Roma - won things during those days of supposedly forced labour. If Peter Crouch ends up even skinnier but with a World Cup winners' medal round his neck, I for one won't be complaining.</p>\u000A<p>His critics - including some on this site - have pointed out that Capello's teams don't always play what Ruud Gullit would call \u201Csheckshy futbol\u201D. But they certainly play winning football, and right now most England fans would find that pretty sexy. His great strength for the England job is not so much his impeccable record as his frequently proven ability to confront players who aren't performing.</p>\u000A<p>Sven-Goran Eriksson and Steve McClaren both seemed to believe that it was enough to pick the best players and let them take it from there. But footballers are simple souls and, just like the rest of us, respond to good management. Of course the players must take their share of the blame for England's poor recent performances, but if they're not playing well it's up to their manager to change things.</p>\u000A<p>Capello himself has said recently: "How can players of the level of Beckham or Owen have performances so different when they play for their national team? It's clear the shirt is very heavy even for those great champions. The manager has a fundamental role to play in this situation. He has to be more of a psychologist than a tactician or a technician.\u201D</p>\u000A<p>And maybe sometimes he needs to be just plain scary. Something has to be done to translate the club form of England's leading players to the international arena, and if that something turns out to be sheer hard work, then make 'em sweat, Fabio.</p>

VThe dogfighting employee: an update
p3016
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/lifeatwork/2007/12/14/the-dogfighting-employee-an-update/
p3017
sg8
(lp3018
sg10
V<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/michael_vick1.jpg" title="michael_vick1.jpg"></a><img vspace="5" align="right" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/michael_vick1.jpg" hspace="5" alt="michael_vick1.jpg" title="michael_vick1.jpg" />You may recall that some months ago <a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/lifeatwork/2007/07/23/dogfighting-sport-and-work-what-should-an-employer-do/"><strong>I blogged about an unfortunate incident involving one of the most outstanding football players in America, Michael Vick</strong></a> (right).</p>\u000A<p>Vick was accused of involvement in dogfighting - an illegal (and extraordinarily cruel) activity.</p>\u000A<p>At the time I invited you to think about the issues raised by the situation for the employer when an employee is charged with a crime:</p>\u000A<p>- Should the employer immediately charge the worker with misconduct and suspend, awaiting trial? Or (especially as here, where the employee is key to the business), regard the worker as innocent unless and until proven otherwise - and allow them to work on in their job?</p>\u000A<p>Well, in this case I can now offer an update - and tell you about the outcome of this horrible story.</p>\u000A<p>The league suspended Vick from playing - so even if the employer had other ideas, he couldn't play this season (at least while charged).</p>\u000A<p>Vick's team - the Atlanta Falcons - have won only three of their 13 games, and are at the bottom of their division (an outcome which has an undoubted financial consequence for the employer).</p>\u000A<p>Vick has been found guilty of running a dogfighting operation and <a target="_blank" href="http://sports.espn.go.com/nfl/news/story?id=3148549"><strong>was this week sentenced to (wait for it) 23 months in jail</strong></a>. Even with things going his way he won't be back to play football next season - and possibly also the season after.</p>\u000A<p>What counted against him (among other things) was the fact that he initially lied about his involvement - and then tested positive for marijuana use in violation of the terms set for his release.</p>\u000A<p>He has been stripped of a $20 million bonus, will lose about $50 million in endorsements, and $71 million in annual salary (for each year that he will be away from the game).</p>\u000A<p>It is perhaps no surprise that Vick has - according to his lawyer - now been diagnosed as clinically depressed.</p>\u000A<p>Wow. How a mistake in life can cost you your career...and more.</p>\u000A<p>But is there anybody who thinks this penalty unfair?</p>\u000A<p><em>Picture: REUTERS</em></p>

VCelebrity beauty and why it matters - at least to them. . .
p3025
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/abouttown/2007/12/14/celebrity-beauty-and-why-it-matters-at-least-to-them/
p3026
sg8
(lp3027
sg10
V<p> <img width="200" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/britney.jpg" height="241" />  <img width="200" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/posh.jpg" height="241" /></p>\u000A<p>In this flash-trash world, of mindless celebrity the only thing that matters, I hate to say it, but it's the truth - is what you look like.</p>\u000A<p>You can wet your pants (Fergie), you can get wasted (Amy Winehouse), you can steal, (Winona Ryder), you can be violent (Naomi Campbell) you can get drug addicted, (Nicole Richie) you can do porn, (Paris Hilton), you can rape (Erroll Flynn), you can be a pederast (Michael Jackson), and yup, you can kill people too (Phil Spectre).</p>\u000A<p>The only thing you cannot do is look bad (weird is OK) and THAT is Britney Spears' real crime.</p>\u000A<p>"Nooooooo..." I hear you intone into your keyboard: ". . .mmmmwhat about Oprah?"</p>\u000A<p>Yes OK, Oprah is no size 10. But Oprah is in a different category because she is so very, very smart.</p>\u000A<p>If Britney didn't look like such an ordinary, normal, frumpy person, if she was as svelte as Paris, and as cool as Mary Kate, sure she'd get dissed for being a lousy mum but she wouldn't face scorn like she is now.<br />\u000AIt's horrible but it's true. The real issue behind her bad press is that she's a hearty s12 and she's got the worst dress sense in the history of Hollywood.</p>\u000A<p>Us human beans have always been visually driven but we are now living in the ultimate appearanc-ist culture and really, it's not so nice.<br />\u000AA variation on this 'appearance crime'-theme is Posh Spice and HER bad press. I feel really sorry for Mrs B. No matter what she does, she gets slammed. It must be frightening picking up the paper because the spin that's put on things is wild. Just recently the reformed Spice Girls appeared for Victoria's Secret with Baby in a dress Britney had worn in 2002 and Geri in a dress Britney had worn in 2004. The girls are dressed by a stylist who would almost definitely have gotten the sack for this "embarrassment" but somehow poor old Mrs B got the blame for having supposedly evilly orchestrated the (ultimately 'who-gives-a-****' ) situation.</p>\u000A<p>I am convinced that:</p>\u000A<p>* If she had nice fake bosoms like everyone else instead of upturned cupcakes on her chest, and . . .</p>\u000A<p>* If she had long hair instead of short hair and</p>\u000A<p>* If she had a smile instead of a stare (she hates her teeth)</p>\u000A<p>she would be loved and lauded. . . .</p>\u000A<p>And she would never have been blamed for that stylist stuff up.</p>\u000A<p>Hell of a shallow world isn't it!</p>\u000A<p><em>(Photos by Reuters)</em></p>

VSir Terry McLean National Sports Journalism Awards
p3034
sg6

V<p>A record 214 entries were received for the 2007 TP McLean Sports Awards on Wednesday the 5th December and the big prize on the night went to The Press reporter Tony Smith, who took out the supreme Air New Zealand Sports Journalist of the Year Award.  Smith also won the Steinlager Award for Newspaper Feature Writing.</p>\u000A<p>Among the throng  were, Grant Fox, Buck Shelford, Steve McDowall, Joe Stanley, John Drake, Coach Sir Brian Lochore, John Hart and Richie Guy, members of the All Blacks team who won the inaugural Rugby World Cup and remain the only All Black team to have won the William Webb Ellis Trophy.  Also at the dinner were members of the 1987 New Zealand Netball team, Julie Coney, Rita Fatialofa-Patolo, Margaret Forsyth, Joan Hodson (Solia), Angela Bell (Pule), Tracy Shortland (Eyrl) and Sandra Gray (Edge), plus Coach Lois Muir DCNZM.OBE., winners of the 1987 World Netball Championships in Glasgow.</p>\u000A<p>The SPARC Lifetime Contribution to Sport through Journalism Award went to radio sport host Brendan Telfer, one of New Zealand\u2019s most respected sports broadcasters.</p>\u000A<p>Two journalists were also made Life Members of the NZSJA \u2013 former cricket and rugby commentator, Colin Snedden, and long time Newstalk ZB sports guru, Barry Holland.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/forsyth-edge.JPG" title="Direct link to file"></p>\u000A<p><img the guests with memories from the 1987</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/muir-edge-coney-shortland.JPG" title="Direct link to file"></p>\u000A<p><img Sports Television<br />\u000AHamish Clark (TV3)<br />\u000AMillennium Hotels Award for Best Sports Column/Opinion<br />\u000ADylan Cleaver (Herald on Sunday)<br />\u000ASteinlager Award for Feature VThe latest music DVDs to arrive through my letterbox
p3041
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/blogonthetracks/2007/12/14/the-latest-music-dvds-to-arrive-through-my-letterbox/
p3042
sg8
(lp3043
sg10
V<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/elvis_1970-275-x-424.jpg" title="elvis_1970-275-x-424.jpg"></a>I seem to be receiving more and more music DVDs lately. I know that in some cases I have specifically requested them. I look forward to getting all the way through the set of <a target="_blank" href="http://www.roadrunnerrecords.com/blabbermouth.net/news.aspx?mode=Article&amp;newsitemID=80325"><strong>AC/DC live clips</strong></a> \u2013 and the <a target="_blank" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0965382/"><strong>Tom Petty documentary</strong></a>. But for every nostalgia trip (<a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/dominionpost/blogs/blogonthetracks/2007/11/28/plugging-back-in-to-nirvana/"><strong>see this polarising post</strong></a>) there are excursions in to the bland world of \u201Cwhy was I sent this?\u201D</p>\u000A<p>Music DVDs are great for me to review on the <a target="_blank" href="http://tvnz.co.nz/view/page/430905/599116"><strong><em>Good Morning</em> TV show</strong></a>; it means I have a ready-made clip without having to beg for beta footage. We can just use the visuals from the disc. Good stuff. But some of the DVDs that arrive just baffle me. I sit through them all though. I am a professional.</p>\u000A<p>So, I thought I\u2019d whip through a few quickly \u2013 ones that I may not get to review elsewhere. Some of these are not (to me) so flash. You might love them. Let\u2019s have a peek\u2026</p>\u000A<p>From the ongoing <em>Live From Austin TX </em>series I sat down to watch the recent offerings (old gigs, but recently released on DVD) from <a target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/John-Mayall-Live-Austin-Texas/dp/B000V6BE1M"><strong>John Mayall</strong></a> and <a target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Polyphonic-Spree-Live-Austin-Texas/dp/B000UDLA4M"><strong>The Polyphonic Spree</strong></a>. Both of these discs are pretty cool. But the gig (in each case) is a mere 50 minutes. With no extras. So \u2013 if John Mayall and/or The Polyphonic Spree are among your favourite artists then you will want these DVDs. The Spree sprawl across the stage, their sweetly manufactured harmonies and hippy-dippy costumes are either to your taste or not. But I rather enjoyed watching this set. I think they\u2019d be cool to see live. John Mayall looks ridiculous in this gig from 1993. He looks like the embarrassing uncle at any 21st. But it\u2019s a reasonably decent blues-rock set.</p>\u000A<p>I have never understood <a target="_blank" href="http://www.nellyfurtado.com/"><strong>Nelly Furtado\u2019s </strong></a>appeal. Watching <a target="_blank" href="http://www.ilikemusic.co.uk/pop/Nelly_Furtado_Do_It_Loose_Concert_DVD-4285"><em><strong>Loose \u2013 The Concert </strong></em></a>didn\u2019t help at all. I hated that song <em>I\u2019m Like a Bird</em>. And when <a target="_blank" href="http://www.penguin.co.uk/static/cs/uk/0/minisites/nickhornby/index.html"><strong>Nick Hornby</strong></a> tried to write in praise of it (<a target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/31-Songs-Nick-Hornby/dp/0141013400"><em><strong>31 Songs</strong></em></a>) it made me hate Nick Hornby. Here Furtado, who has had a big year, and basically made herself over as a pop star (again), comes across as <strong>Gloria Estefan </strong>before the crash (in all senses of the word). I wish the rhythm really would get her.</p>\u000A<p><img vspace="5" align="right" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/elvis_1970-275-x-424.jpg" hspace="5" alt="elvis_1970-275-x-424.jpg" title="elvis_1970-275-x-424.jpg" /><a target="_blank" href="http://www.elvis.com/"><strong>Elvis Presley </strong></a>is pretty cool. It is easy to say that he was not a good musician, but that\u2019s missing the point. Big time. Elvis really was the greatest \u2013 at what he did. He rocked. It took me years to really get my head around how superb he was \u2013 at his best \u2013 but I\u2019m there now and one of my favourite music DVDs is <a target="_blank" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0065687/"><em><strong>Elvis \u2013 That\u2019s The Way It Is.</strong></em></a> Yes, I know that every year some record company folk decide there must be a way to repackage and re-sell The King. And it seems to (usually) work. This year there was another greatest hits CD. And <a target="_blank" href="http://www.elvis.com.au/presley/dvd/elvis_the_king_dvd_19.shtml"><em><strong>Elvis: The King of Rock\u2019n\u2019Roll</strong></em></a> is the accompanying DVD. I rather enjoyed this \u2013 to me it was a bit of a one-watch though. Thirty songs are shown, from early promo clips through to the classic <a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elvis_Presley's_'68_Comeback_Special"><em><strong>\u201968 Comeback Special</strong></em></a> and my aforementioned favourite show/film (from 1970). If you never liked Elvis I guess it is obvious that you should pray that no one gives you this DVD for Christmas. If you know someone who likes Elvis (and statistics suggest that is most definitely the case) then you could do worse than offer this sampler-DVD to the one you love who loves Elvis Presley.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.manchestereveningnews.co.uk/entertainment/music/s/1025694_keane_live_dvd_universal"><em><strong>Keane Live</strong></em></a> was next in the DVD player. Not keen.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.davidbowie.com/"><strong>David Bowie</strong></a> has had a remarkable career \u2013 but two words tend to put fear in the heart of even the most ardent support of the erstwhile Ziggy, the former Thin White Duke. And no, I don\u2019t mean <a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tin_Machine"><strong>Tin Machine</strong></a>. I mean two <em>other</em> words. <em>Glass Spider</em>. Finally the <a target="_blank" href="http://www.dvdmg.com/davidbowieglassspider.shtml"><strong>1987 tour comes to DVD </strong></a>(what, there was actually demand for this?). I remember watching the video and not understanding it at all. It is almost hilariously kitsch to watch this show now, 20 years on. What has he thinking? The dancers look like they were modelled on extras from <a target="_blank" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0080120/"><em><strong>The Warriors</strong></em></a> \u2013 all this from a guy deemed cutting edge? <a target="_blank" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0091369/"><em><strong>Labyrinth</strong></em></a> must have rotted his brain. When <a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Frampton"><strong>Peter Frampton</strong></a> is playing guitar on stage \u2013 and it is not the worst thing happening\u2026well, it is time to look elsewhere for answers, right? But, if, like me, you are a bit of Bowie fan, you might still like a look at this. Just don\u2019t look too closely. One watch should be the rule here.</p>\u000A<p>This year I had the displeasure to hear an album called <em>Life in Cartoon Motion</em> by some berk named <a target="_blank" href="http://www.mikasounds.com/uk.php"><strong>Mika</strong></a>. This guy seems keen to try to take the worst elements of <a target="_blank" href="http://www.scissorsisters.com/intro/"><strong>The Scissor Sisters </strong></a>and <a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Darkness"><strong>The Darkness </strong></a>and prove that he can make something even worse! No-Brainer, right? Instead of being a post-millennial <strong>Bee Gees</strong> and/or a post-millennial <strong>Meatloaf</strong>, Mika has desires to be the new <strong>Freddy Mercury</strong>. This is so blatantly obvious that in the interview segments on the DVD I am about to mention he talks about how he is not just a one-man <strong>Queen</strong> revival. Which pretty much guarantees you that he is in fact a one-man Queen revival \u2013 so, we get to the DVD: <strong><em><a target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.com/Mika-Live-Cartoon-Motion/dp/B000WOYRJE">Live in Cartoon Motion</a></em></strong> is Mika live in concert playing the hits from his album. It is really horrible. He also covers <strong>The Eurhythmics\u2019 </strong><em>Sweet Dreams (Are Made of This) </em>and manages to make detractors forget about <strong>Marilyn Manson\u2019s </strong>decimation of <em>Sweet Dreams</em>. The painful falsetto prancing over cheap ivory-tinkling is a gimmick that is swiftly worn out. I wouldn\u2019t send this DVD to my worst enemy for Christmas (it would be pointless anyway, sending Mika a copy of his own DVD, right?).</p>\u000A<p>Next up I watched the <a target="_blank" href="http://www.cduniverse.com/productinfo.asp?pid=7519686"><em><strong>Concert For Diana </strong></em></a>\u2013 a 2-DVD set chronicling the concert that Princes Harry and William put on for their deceased mother (\u201Cthe people\u2019s princess\u201D). There are some okay songs/performances here \u2013 but it is a long haul. A hard workout \u2013 thank god for the skip button or I never would have made it. At least five hours of performances were economically skipped down to about 35 minutes of highlights in my swift viewing. <strong>Duran Duran </strong>shows no feeling for the situation at all by singing <em>Wild Boys</em>. I thought they were going to sing <em>Hungry Like a Wolf </em>and then dedicate it to the rabid paparazzi at the scene of the crash. What, too soon? Ten years on? Of course <strong>Elton John </strong>kicked things off and he played <em>Your Song</em>. Like a total cheese.</p>\u000A<p>Then there were pointless songs by <a target="_blank" href="http://fergie.blackeyedpeas.com/"><strong>Fergie</strong></a>, <a target="_blank" href="http://www.lilyallenmusic.com/"><strong>Lily Allen</strong></a>, Nelly Furtado (ugh, I had to watch her on DVD twice in one weekend!) and <a target="_blank" href="http://www.anastacia.com/"><strong>Anastacia</strong></a>. Some of the old heads came through. <strong>Rod Stewart </strong>was great, launching into <em>Maggie May</em> straight away and following it up with <em>Baby Jane</em>. <strong>Bryan Ferry </strong>was all class \u2013 as he almost always is. Then the rot really set in with a ridiculous medley of ridiculous songs from the ridiculous pen of the rather, erm, ridiculous <a target="_blank" href="http://www.reallyuseful.com/rug/html/index.htm"><strong>Andrew Lloyd-Webber</strong></a>. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.thebubbleburst.co.uk/bb.php?entry=Jason%20Donovan"><strong>Jason Donovan</strong></a> and <a target="_blank" href="http://www.donny.com/announcements.pl?cmd=view&amp;aid=235"><strong>Donny Osmond </strong></a>battled it out to prove who was the bigger has-been in their duelling renditions of songs from <em>Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</em>. Any dream indeed! They\u2019re both still hanging on\u2026</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.diddy.com/"><strong>P Diddy </strong></a>tried to remain relevant \u2013 pointless considering <a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kanye_West"><strong>Kanye West</strong></a> was there to usurp him (again). And there was a good comedy-spot by <a target="_blank" href="http://www.rickygervais.com/"><strong>Ricky Gervais </strong></a>singing that song <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9JitDWQI9qc"><strong>that David Brent does in the episode of <em>The Office</em> when he sabotages the team-training session</strong></a>. Gold.</p>\u000A<p>But what a long-winded DVD to sit through; boring tributes to Diana\u2019s amazing humanity ring out while roadies nearly as old as the members of <a target="_blank" href="http://www.statusquo.co.uk/"><strong>Status Quo </strong></a>plod along behind amps. Here\u2019s a newsflash: <strong>Princess Anne</strong> has done twice as much for humanitarian causes \u2013 and she\u2019s competed at the Olympic Games! (A royal doing some real work for once.) Just because she happens to look more like the horse she rides than any human should, she seems to be written off. Sad.</p>\u000A<p>I was sent a DVD by <a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Rieu"><strong>Andre Rieu</strong></a>. This guy is someone I have avoided for years. I have happily sold his material when I worked in music stores. I have been sent copies of his CDs and always passed them on without a listen. But a DVD? This piqued my curiosity. I wish it hadn\u2019t. I next watched <a target="_blank" href="http://www.moviestars.co.nz/DVDs/1551177.html"><em><strong>Andre Rieu in Wonderland</strong></em></a>. Oh my! This guy is a nut. A total cheese \u2013 with a smug look as he saws away rather mundanely at his violin while all around him it is as if Dorothy has gone missing and the rest of the cast of the original <em>Wizard of Oz</em> have been dug up, fed ecstasy pills and been forced to trudge through all their worst moments, being told to make it count this time! It\u2019s music/muzak for people with no clue. I wish I had the minutes of my life back between pressing play and pressing eject (and that is only about 13 minutes in total).</p>\u000A<p>As with the <em>Live from Austin TX</em> series, another ongoing set of DVDs that I like to keep in vague touch with is the <em>Live At Montreux </em>concerts. The Montreux Jazz Festival often has very little to do with actual jazz, spreading out to take in funk, soul and pop artists. Recently I received <a target="_blank" href="http://www.gpstore.co.nz/DVDs/1551714.html"><strong>the Jamiroquai entry</strong></a> \u2013 a live set from 2003\u2019s festival. I had always thought that Jamiroquai would be a great live act \u2013 I\u2019ve never been a fan of the band, but I\u2019ve never exactly hated them. I started off enjoying this concert, but was bored very swiftly. The first two Jamiroquai albums were not too bad \u2013 certainly better than anything <strong>Stevie Wonder</strong> was doing at the time (which is essentially what the JK albums were, unaccredited Stevie Wonder attempts). But I guess the problem was the band continued to release those same two albums every two years for over a decade. This gig is not bad \u2013 but it drags on a little toward the end.</p>\u000A<p>From 2005, in the same series, I also watched <a target="_blank" href="http://shop.mtv.com/Isaac-Hayes--Live-at-Montreux-2005-Concerts--nf-_stcVVproductId21227982VVcatId421318VVviewprod.htm"><strong>the Isaac Hayes gig</strong></a>. This is pretty cool. It takes a while for Mr <em>Chocolate Salty Balls</em> to really wind up \u2013 starting the gig with some pretty boring material. But then the Bacharach and Jimmy Webb covers kick in \u2013 and of course the <em>Theme from Shaft</em>. And it\u2019s a rocking-sweet soul-funk affair. A good way to end \u2013 proof that not all was wasted looking through these DVDs.</p>\u000A<p>I am so thrilled that DVD players come with skip buttons, or I never would have made it.</p>\u000A<p>That\u2019s the latest batch that made it through the letterbox. There are more sitting in piles. I will get to them soon.</p>

VTime to waste some time
p3050
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/hitlist/2007/12/14/time-to-waste-some-time/
p3051
sg8
(lp3052
sg10
V<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/gta1.jpg" title="fsda"></a><img border="3" vspace="6" align="right" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/gta1.jpg" hspace="6" alt="fsda" />A new <strong>Jay-Z</strong> mash-up, brand spanking Portishead songs, a ditzy blonde, new videos from <strong>Radiohead</strong> and <strong>The Killers</strong>, and trailers for <em>Sex and the City</em>, <em>Grand Theft Auto IV</em> and, erm, <em>American Gladiators</em>.</p>\u000A<p>It's all here in the <strong>Best Links of the Week:</strong></p>\u000A<p><strong>1. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.rockstargames.com/IV/">GTA IV trailers</a>:</strong> Three trailers have been released for <strong>Grand Theft Auto IV</strong>, which is due for release sometime between February and April next year. That's not very exact, but it looks awesome.</p>\u000A<p><strong>2. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zU-Aa_nXV0U">Slusho commercial</a>:</strong> Who knows what it all means, but <strong>JJ Abrams</strong> is taking this interactive internet promotion thing to new highs. And <strong><a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/hitlist/2007/12/12/an-open-letter-to-jj-abrams/">lows</a></strong>. Or he's taken way too much acid. </p>\u000A<p><strong>3.<em> <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TKtaogEfppU">A Great Big Sled</a></em></strong><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TKtaogEfppU"><strong> - The Killers</strong></a><strong>:</strong> <strong>The Killers</strong> have recorded a Christmas song with accompanying festive video. A B-sides album, and now this? The only question is: Why, Brandon, why?</p>\u000A<p><strong>4. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Py-cf0Ktj3k"><em>American Gladiators</em> trailer</a>:</strong> Remember that stupid mid-90s show in which normal people like you and me would try and knock ex-wrestlers off benches with padded sticks? Yeah, it's back.</p>\u000A<p><strong>5. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VwnQO9Du19Q">American Zeppelin mash-up</a>:</strong> <strong>DJ Doc Rok</strong> has done a <em>Grey Album</em>, mixing <strong>Jay-Z's</strong> <em>American Gangster</em> with a smattering of <strong>Led Zeppelin's</strong> biggest and best. Download the full album <strong><a target="_blank" href="http://www.sendspace.com/pro/dl/jre9v3">here</a></strong>.</p>\u000A<p><strong>6. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kk2-ntNyZaY"><em>Sex and the City: The Movie</em> trailer</a>:</strong> Okay girls, here you go. It's all there: <strong>Carrie</strong> and the girls, New York, a wedding, crazy outfits and <strong>Mr Big</strong>. Save your new shoe-buying expedition though - it's not out till May.</p>\u000A<p><strong>7. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_lmgNqFuXwc">Is Europe a Country</a>:</strong> <strong>Kellie Pickler</strong> gives blondes a bad name when she says 'I thought Europe was a country' then goes on to ask 'Is France a country?' on game show <em>Are You Smarter Than A 10-Year-Old</em>? It turns out she's not.</p>\u000A<p><strong>8. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UKrsBVFsfIQ"><em>Jigsaw Falling Into Place</em> - Radiohead</a>:</strong> A nifty video recorded on helmet cam from <strong>Radiohead's</strong> fantastic album <em>In Rainbows</em>. Get your orders in for the CD release, out December 31.</p>\u000A<p><strong>9. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9oYDBtCN-hk"><em>Crank That</em> - Kosha Boy</a>:</strong> The jury is out on whether this is just another Soulja Boy pisstake or a hilarious Jewish version. You can make your own mind up.</p>\u000A<p><strong>10. <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tVaJErZ2xAE"><em>Machine Gun</em> - Portishead</a>:</strong> The best new track unveiled by much-loved British trip-hop band Portishead during a recent concert. They also played four other newbies: <strong><a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ISBUaMymjj0">Mystic</a></strong>, <strong><em><a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CWNslMS3eEI">Hunter</a></em></strong>, <a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MhMVjJyg71M"><strong><em>Wicca</em></strong> </a>and <strong><em><a target="_blank" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1TIphtLZLw4">Peaches</a></em></strong>. Welcome back, Beth and co.</p>\u000A<p>Got any you'd like to add to the list?</p>

V<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/650-skyhawk.jpg" title="Taking precautions"></p>\u000A<p><img border="1" vspace="5" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/650-skyhawk.jpg" hspace="5" alt="Taking precautions" title="Taking precautions" /></p>\u000A<p></a></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/650-skyhawk.jpg" title="Taking precautions"></a>Seeing the shrink-wrapped <a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4322648a11.html"><strong>Skyhawks</strong></a> reminded me of the all but obsolete technology I have squirrelled away in my bedroom.</p>\u000A<p>There's an Apple Powermac G4, circa 2000; it's still a good machine, albeit not a slowish one, but with very little resale value.</p>\u000A<p>I've also got my old digital camera; it takes fine pictures, but doesn't have the sort of megapixel specs that people are so hung up on these days.</p>\u000A<p>Under my bed are several Walkmen in various states of repair, but who plays tapes these days?</p>\u000A<p>I also have a mountain of CDs that I'm unlikely to ever play again and a wardrobe full of clothes that will only see daylight if fashions and my body shape revert to the way things were in 1987.</p>\u000A<p>Okay, fashion is heading that way, but short of me contacting a nasty illness I can't see myself taking part in any kind of retro revolution.</p>\u000A<p>Actually it's the same with the Skyhawks.</p>\u000A<p>The only way they'll be useful in warfare again is if the UN bans all weapons designed after 1970.</p>\u000A<p>Perhaps they'll be dusted off if someone remakes <a target="_blank" href="http://www.moria.co.nz/sf/sleepingdogs.htm"><strong><em>Sleeping Dogs</em></strong></a>.</p>\u000A<p>Oh well, they look kind of cool bagged up in their skin-tight latex sheaths, in a postmodern art/bondage way.</p>

VHa ha! Nelson makes his move
p3068
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/checkraise/2007/12/14/ha-ha-nelson-makes-his-move/
p3069
sg8
(lp3070
sg10
V<p>Great to see Lee Nelson advance to day two at the APPT finale in Sydney yesterday.</p>\u000A<p>However, Waikato's James Honeybone went to the rail early on day 1b on a day of some spectacular hands at the PokerStars-sponsored tournament.</p>\u000A<p>Lee ended the day with $93,500 in chips - good enough for 25th spot among the 72 players remaining after two days, with day 1c on the cards today.</p>\u000A<p>Among the chip leaders, baby, was his fellow Team PokerStars member Scotty Nguyen with $250,400.<br />\u000ALee was all in with the remainder of his chips yesterday with Qd-Qh against Julian Powell, who made the call with As-Qs.</p>\u000A<p>That made the Kiwi a 65% fave and the board of Js-9c-8c 6h 4d meant that held up.</p>\u000A<p>Soon after doubling up, Lee picked up another big pot when he moved with Ad-Qs on a queen-high flop. His opponent tabled Ks-Qc and the 2006 Aussie Millions winner was off and running.<br />\u000A <br />\u000AJames perished when he entered a battle of the blinds with Kenny Ng.</p>\u000A<p>Ng raised from the BB to $1000 and James called to see an intriguing flop of Ad-Kh-Qs.</p>\u000A<p>James checked, Ng fbet $1200 and James made the call. The turn was the 4s and Ng fired again, this time for $5000 and James again flat-called.</p>\u000A<p>The river fell 10s and James pushed all in for his remaining $10,000. Ng made the crying call and when James revealed Kd-8s, Ng's set was good for the big pot.</p>\u000A<p>So for knocking out Waikato's finest, and for committing a monster crime against humanity for being seen at the table with a Manchester United cap on, Ng is in danger of surpassing Shawn Sheikahn at the bottom of the CROPPs.</p>\u000A<p>Both Lee and James were interviewed early in the day - the clips are on the page <a href="http://www.pokernews.com/live-reporting/video-gallery/" title="video">here</a>.</p>\u000A<p>There were a number of exciting hands played out yesterday.</p>\u000A<p>Aussie Billy Sukkar, a cousin of Joe and Tony Hachem who featured at the Aussie Millions won by Nelson, had his aces cracked by 7d-3d and sent to the rail.</p>\u000A<p>After two players limped into the pot, one from the small blind, Sukkar made it $900 to go from the big blind and got two callers.</p>\u000A<p>The flop came Qd-8d-6d and both the small blind and Sukkar checked to the initial limper, who led out with $3000. The small blind got out of the way and Sukkar called.</p>\u000A<p>The turn brought the As, giving Sukkar the top set, and he checked to his opponent who moved all in, having Sukkar covered.</p>\u000A<p>Sukkar called and his opponent revealed his made flush and the 2s on the river didn't help the young Aussie who left the tourney with a set of aces.</p>\u000A<p>The following was a personal highlight that I'm sure all home game players will love - we call it "A Short Smack moment".</p>\u000A<p>In a multi-way raised pot, a short-stack came over the top and pushed the rest of his stack in pre-flop. It was folded around quickly to an unknown internet qualifier who appeared to be giving the decision much deliberation.</p>\u000A<p>The player was not aware that the previous players had already folded and didn't realize the action was on him. After close to five minutes of apparent deep thought, the dealer called a tournament director over and called "time" on the player, giving him 60 seconds to act on his hand. The internet qualifier suddenly realised that "time" was being called on himself and apologetically threw his card into the muck.</p>\u000A<p>That's just too funny... I can just picture the net noob sitting there thinking "Man, no wonder I play on the net, these dudes take yonks!"<br />\u000A </p>\u000A<p>Van Marcus rode a mid-day rollercoaster when he had pocket Qs cracked by two players who made runner-runner straights.</p>\u000A<p>The very next hand Marcus raised from the small blind and was not surprisingly adjudged by most at the table to be nearing full tilt.</p>\u000A<p>The Aussie fired three barrels on a board of 8s-7s-3d Kh 4s and got action from one other player, who mucked when Marcus flipped over pocket aces.</p>\u000A<p>Later in the day, an uknown player with pocket rockets hit a flop of As-5s-10c when up against the pocket queens of Sol Bergren.</p>\u000A<p>But he became the second "Sukkar" to leave with a set of aces when the turn fell Kh and the river was a Jc.</p>\u000A<p>In another highlighted hand, Francisicus Dekkers was all in pre-flop with 6h6s against AsQc, makig him a slight fave (54% v 45%).</p>\u000A<p>The flop of Jh-8s-10s basically switched those numbers around and when a Js came on the turn, Dekkers' rival had a mahoosive pile of outs.</p>\u000A<p>Aussie pro Mark Vos reckoned Dekkers' opponent had an amazing 25 outs heading into the river but Dekkers escaped a bullet on the river for his sixes to hold.</p>\u000A<p>Last night's home game saw a reduced field as a number of the usual suspects chose other pursuits.</p>\u000A<p>Monty, aka The Big Unit, has a black mark against his name and will never win a major if he doesn't bring his clubs. The Mentor also chose intoxication instead of mixing it with poker like he normally does while Poochie continued his Lord Lucan impersonation and Short Smack was doing his own Gaylord Focker impersonation in a home game of Meet the Parents.</p>\u000A<p>I played like a donk in the first of two four-handed games between me, The Gladiator, Matski and Prem.</p>\u000A<p>Getting way too cute and trying to trap with good hands, I simply gave free cards to my opponents and fell into the hole myself before being first out. Matski eventually took the cash after going heads-up with Glad.</p>\u000A<p>I turned things around in the second game though, playing a game more suited to four-handed poker but did trap nicely when it fit myhand and the board.</p>\u000A<p>After a fun period of all ins and calls with Blind Prem-on, I took a monster pot from Matski with a straight made on the turn and ended heads-up with our host again.</p>\u000A<p>Made an aggressive call to end it all when I held 4d-2d in the big blind and Glad limped in. The flop fell 9d-5c-2s, I bet out with bottom pair about half the pot and got called.</p>\u000A<p>The turn was a Kd and I bet out about two-thirds the pot, only to be re-raised all in. Time to make a read.</p>\u000A<p>I didn't put him on a king and felt his push was designed to move me off as I'd been taking down pots with raises since starting heads-up. I had a 2-1 chip advantage and if I made the call I'd still have enough left behind to play with if beaten.</p>\u000A<p>While I wasn't getting the right pot odds, I did have the nine outs with the flush draw (if he had two diamonds, so be it, I'm not laying down a flush heads-up), another two with the ducks and possibly three more with the fours.</p>\u000A<p>Not only that, but I thought there was probably a 25/30% chance that Glad was making a move with nothing, maybe Q or J high so that had to be factored in with the outs.</p>\u000A<p>I decided to gamble and take a chance to collect the cash there and then - right ....... there. I made the call and the river was a lovely four as Glad revealed 9-7 and I'd finally won one after what seemed like a long barren spell.</p>\u000A<p>Enjoy the weekend<br />\u000AShuffle up and deal</p>

VLooking back on fashion for 2007
p3077
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/catwalktalk/2007/12/14/looking-back-on-fashion-for-2007/
p3078
sg8
(lp3079
sg10
V<p>Its not all done and dusted yet - but since the year of 2007 is almost over, it's probably a good time to reminisce on the events past.</p>\u000A<p>For the fashion world, no one could've expected what events and trends came to be. The trends varied from structured, flowing, masculine, hobo (yet again), rave (thanks to Jeremy Scott), punk, and preppy. Oh and billboard Tees. Cheers House of Holland.</p>\u000A<p>There were <em>Star Wars-</em>style C-3PO Balenciaga leggings designed by the ridiculously talented Nicolas Ghesquière for the Spring 2007 collection, retailing for a cool $159,000 - which brings back the nice and (usually forgotten) idea that money is not an object when it comes to style, and that not everybody needs to blow money on "vintage" pieces to call themselves unique.</p>\u000A<p><img vspace="5" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/10m.jpg" hspace="5" alt="10m.jpg" title="10m.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p>There was Hermes, who created their classic Birkin with Crocodile skin and diamonds retailing for $148,000, and artist Damien Hirst, who made a <strong>life-size human skull</strong> encrusted with 8601 diamonds which sold for a reported $122 million.</p>\u000A<p><img vspace="5" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/1724248531_d87fba7bae_o.jpg" hspace="5" alt="1724248531_d87fba7bae_o.jpg" title="1724248531_d87fba7bae_o.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p>As for fashion shows, Fendi took the cake with their $10,000,000 show, which was situated on none other than the <strong>Great Wall of China</strong>. Designer Karl Lagerfeld was also quick to point out: "The wall is built to be a runway, huh? They don't have to use it for fighting Mongolians anymore; now they can use it for fashion."As for NZ, who could forget our fashion week? I know. Me too.</p>\u000A<p><img vspace="5" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/1112912177_a9fe12a1aa.jpg" hspace="5" alt="1112912177_a9fe12a1aa.jpg" title="1112912177_a9fe12a1aa.jpg" /></p>\u000A<p>It was also interesting to see the emerging trend of designers using the run-down dregs of celebrities as muses for campaigns, collections and media - and I'm not talking Lorraine Downes for Petrena Miller. I'm thinking more along the lines of <strong>Karl Lagerfeld and Courtney Love</strong>. The woman was so high she couldn't even tell she was wearing a fake! And now the legendary designer finds inspiration in the woman? See this is what I'm talking about when I say that this year has been highly unpredictable.</p>\u000A<p>Then there was the "Skinny Debate". C'mon people! Do you think models are paid to sit on fat asses? No. They're paid to be skinny. They always have been and they always will be. If ads looked better shot with average-sized people - then chances are the models would all be out of work.</p>\u000A<p>The year 2007 also lost one of the most fashion-forward people in the business: Isabella Blow. Her signature style was the inspiration for the exhibition which came to our part of the world with "When Phillip met Isabella" at the NewDowse in Wellington.</p>\u000A<p>And for 2008? Well after this year all I can really say "who knows"? But out with the old and in with the new!</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/1112912177_a9fe12a1aa.jpg" title="1112912177_a9fe12a1aa.jpg"></a></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/1724248531_d87fba7bae_o.jpg" title="1724248531_d87fba7bae_o.jpg"></a></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2007/12/10m.jpg" title="10m.jpg"></a></p>

V<p><img width="275" height="235" align="right" src="http://www.dropkicks.co.nz/modules/htmlarea/Xinha/plugins/ImageManager/image_uploads/_2007_12/V7hcVBAH.jpg" alt="V7hcVBAH.jpg" />The <a href="http://mlb.mlb.com/news/article.jsp?ymd=20071213&amp;content_id=2324860&amp;vkey=news_mlb&amp;fext=.jsp&amp;c_id=mlb">Mitchell Report</a> is out.</p>\u000A<p>I know you\u2019re thinking, \u201Cthe what?\u201D, but the Mitchell Report may end up being a giant kick in the nutsack to Major League Baseball (or not depending on how much lying happens).</p>\u000A<p>Several high-profile, superstar-caliber players were among those named in­ of former Sen. George Mitchell's report concerning use of performance-enhancing drugs in Major League Baseball. The report was the product of a 21-month, multimillion dollar investigation that could shape decisions, prompt punitive actions against active players, and usher in the next era of the sport.</p>\u000A<p>Free agent Roger Clemens, Andy Pettitte of the New York Yankees, Miguel Tejada of the Houston Astros, Eric Gagne of the Milwaukee Brewers and Paul Lo Duca of the Washington Nationals were among the most prominent former and current All-Stars to be mentioned in the lengthy report, (and by lengthy I mean 409 pages!). The report also contains multiple exhibits, including evidence of signed checks, handwritten notes and shipping receipts.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.theonion.com/content/news/destruction_of_national_pastime"><img width="222" height="319" align="left" src="http://www.dropkicks.co.nz/modules/htmlarea/Xinha/plugins/ImageManager/image_uploads/_2007_12/Barry_Bonds_3.jpg" alt="Barry_Bonds_3.jpg" />­</a>The report was delivered with the backdrop of Barry Bonds having just pleaded not guilty last week in a San Francisco federal court on four counts of perjury and one count of obstruction of justice. This is conjunction with BALCO and we know how well that ended for <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/topNews/idUSL1220829120071212">Marion Jones</a>.</p>\u000A<p>But the report is not all doom and horse juice. It also contains a number of recommendations for MLB to move forward.</p>\u000A<p>Have I read it yet? Did I mention 409 pages? I have just got to the end of the list of contents.</p>\u000A<p>But for your reading pleasure the MLB have <a href="http://files.mlb.com/mitchrpt.pdf">uploaded the pdf</a> (6.47Mb) so you can download and read at your leisure (apprently they are working on an easy clickable version too).</p>

VFriday Miscellany: Sloon, Murali and Hamilton
p3132
sg6
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/sidelineslogger/2007/12/14/friday-miscellany-sloon-murali-and-hamilton/
p3133
sg8
(lp3134
sg10
V<p><img border="5" vspace="5" align="right" width="257" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/images/images/689826.jpg?w=300&amp;h=308" hspace="5" height="261" />Right, I am getting off the fence - I was initially wondering what we were playing at firing up the thunderbolt thrower <strong>Shaun "</strong>Sloon"<strong> Tait</strong> but after <a target="_blank" href="http://content-sl.cricinfo.com/slc/content/image/269003.html"><strong>looking here</strong></a> there's no doubt his "bowling" action is questionable.</p>\u000A<p>A wonderful irony with a Sri Lankan, <strong>Roshan Mahanama </strong>at the top table as match referee in Adelaide for tonight's clash. Mahanama is no fan of Australian pace bowling, and one person not on his Christmas card list is caravan-lover Glenn McGrath. In his autobiography, the Sri Lankan <a target="_blank" href="http://www.rediff.com/cricket/2001/jul/31maha.htm"><strong>accused</strong></a> the Australian paceman of calling Sanath Jayasuriya a "black monkey" in the 1995/96 World Series. McGrath, predictably, denied the accusation.</p>\u000A<p>Speaking of alleged chuckers and Sri Lankans, <strong>Muttiah Muralitharan </strong>has been honoured with a (dreadful) song by Aussie-based Lankan Alston Koch. Brace yourself when you download <em>Murali</em> from <a target="_blank" href="http://mcricket.mobi/download_song.jsp?id=18D8136CAAB5E00A455AAE2042086666"><strong>here</strong></a>. We will also be reviewing it on The BYC <a target="_blank" href="http://beigebrigade.co.nz/loop/byc/"><strong>podcast</strong></a> this week. According to World Music Central, Alston has been "a leading Sri Lankan musician since the 1960s...Koch performed at all the well-known night clubs in Ceylon including the Coconut Grove in Colombo". Sounds a bit like <strong>John Rowles</strong>.</p>\u000A<p>A <em>Sideline Slogger </em>reader with impeccable credentials has done the economic analysis and reckons <strong>Dan Vettori</strong>, <strong>Jacob Oram </strong>and <strong>Jeetan Patel </strong>are our best bets for bowling at the death after running the numbers over recent efforts in the last 10 overs. According to <a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/sidelineslogger/2007/12/06/the-underarm-wker-series/"><strong>The Economist</strong></a>, X-Box fan Mark Gillespie's record is not as good as any of these three and he's more expensive than other contenders, Scotty Styris and Kyle Mills.</p>\u000A<p><img border="5" vspace="5" align="right" width="351" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Fonterra_Facility_Near_Hamilton.jpg/800px-Fonterra_Facility_Near_Hamilton.jpg" hspace="5" height="253" />Quote of the week is from <em>The Daily Star </em>in Bangladesh: "The team bus took the Tigers to <strong>Hamilton</strong> to their Novotel Tainui Hotel...past breathtaking greenery, lovely single storey houses and livestock grazing the valleys on both sides of the road like you find in picture books. Adding to the atmosphere was the absence of a siren blowing police or security escort which just would not have fitted with the level of tranquility around."</p>\u000A<p>Finally, here is an <strong>In-form New Zealand XI</strong>, selected solely from those playing in the State Championship domestic competition. The <em>Sideline Slogger </em>joins them in banging on the selectors' doors and yelling: "Come on!" The XI is: Matthew Bell, Aaron Redmond, Peter Fulton, Greg Hay, Greg Todd, Neal Parlane, Reece Young, Andre Adams, Brandon Hiini, Bradley Scott, Andy McKay. Honourable mention: Charlie Shreck (England). Bell and Adams are stitching together increasingly compelling cases to be selected ahead of incumbents Michael Papps and Iain O'Brien.</p>

VTwo drunk backbenchers
p3141
sg6
Vhttp://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=869
p3142
sg8
(lp3143
sg10
V<p>A mate of mine had a rather interesting run-in last night with a couple of drunken Tory backbenchers. Here's what happened:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p>Last night I was at the Malthouse in Courtenay Place having a few beers with some mates when who should walk into the bar but a couple of National Party backbenchers. We struck up a conversation, and an enlightening one it was. Both Nats had clearly had a few and the rookie\u2019s tongue was looser than I would have thought wise (I noticed his more experienced colleague was far more reserved).</p>\u000A<p>He readily agreed that John Key comes across as \u2018a bit smug but he\u2019s a tough bugger and he works us like dogs, as he should\u2019.  We were assured that \u2018she\u2019 (Clark, presumably) would \u2018knock that smugness out of him in the campaign\u2019. </p>\u000A<p>We were then told that \u2018John doesn\u2019t really know what he wants to do if (when, hah!) he becomes Prime Minister and he certainly hasn\u2019t told us!\u2019 But, then \u2018He\u2019s new to politics; he shouldn\u2019t know what he wants. He\u2019s just got to hit the right notes with the public\u2019. I gained a striking impression that power was being sought for its own sake, not to make a better New Zealand.  </p>\u000A<p>Searching for some glimmer of a vision, the Nats were asked about where they thought the country should head. \u2018Singapore\u2019 was the answer: we should be looking to a city-state on the world\u2019s busiest shipping strait that is run as a mix of autocracy and plutocracy as the model.  Every mention of vision or policy was solely limited to economics: people appeared in the frame merely as commodities and factors of production.</p>\u000A<p>So, maintain and fortify privilege for those who have it, that\u2019s name of the game, and do so by \u2018hitting the right notes\u2019.</p>\u000A<p>\u2018John\u2019, we were informed, \u2018could hit the right notes about 85% of the time\u2019 much better than \u2018English, who only gets it right 65% of the time\u2019 (note who gets first names, the faction this backbencher sat in was clear).</p>\u000A<p>At this point the slightly nervous-looking, more experienced politician decided it was time they extracted themselves before his friend started telling us intimate details of caucus sessions. We were left amused but more than a little concerned that this is the true face of the National party behind Key\u2019s grinning façade.</p></blockquote>\u000A<p>I imagine the rookie had more than his hangover to worry about this morning.</p>\u000A<p class="akst_link"><a href="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=869&amp;akst_action=share-this" title="E-mail this, post to del.icio.us, etc." id="akst_link_869" class="akst_share_link" rel="nofollow">Share This</a>\u000A</p>

VNational reopens Selwyn race
p3157
sg6
Vhttp://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=868
p3158
sg8
(lp3159
sg10
V<p>Local Nats don't want David Carter as their candidate for Selwyn.</p>\u000A<p>Looks like the threats, intimidation and bullying tactics used to get him the candidacy have backfired for him. Carter (himself a three time loser to Labour's Ruth Dyson in Banks Peninsula) has a history of bagging other candidates within his party.</p>\u000A<p>He said of Brian Connell, when selected for Rakaia in 2002, that National "didn't get a hell of a good line-up of candidates... they weren't bad but there was nobody who was a stunner" (Chch Press, 3 Oct 2006).</p>\u000A<p>Well the local party people didn't toss Brian Connell back quite as fast as they're trying to bin David Carter - they're right to of course because in his own words - he isn't a stunner either.</p>\u000A<p>My bet is that John Key will still want him to win the selection and that Carter will be forced on the electorate against the wishes of the local Nats. Democracy - National style.</p>\u000A<p>From the <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/thepress/4323181a19720.html">Press</a> this morning:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><strong>National reopens Selwyn race</strong></p>\u000A<p>National MP David Carter will battle up to 12 rival candidates for the Selwyn seat after the party's board agreed to an embarrassing selection rerun.</p>\u000A<p>Nominations for electorates across the country have closed, but National president Judy Kirk said yesterday the board had decided to reopen the Selwyn contest in February after 35 party members lodged a formal complaint...</p>\u000A<p>It is understood the candidates were warned several front-bench National MPs would publicly campaign for Carter to get the nod if they put their names forward.</p>\u000A<p>Carter's colleagues felt such a senior MP should not have to face a selection battle against newcomers...</p>\u000A<p>In its complaint to the board, the disgruntled group of party members said Carter should have known the selection process was flawed. "His future as a Cabinet minister will often put him under the spotlight and, if this is a sign of his true judgment, then we may be headed for turbulent times with him as a minister of the Crown," the letter says...</p></blockquote>\u000A<p class="akst_link"><a href="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=868&amp;akst_action=share-this" title="E-mail this, post to del.icio.us, etc." id="akst_link_868" class="akst_share_link" rel="nofollow">Share This</a>\u000A</p>

VNZ leads the world on climate change in Bali
p3171

Vhttp://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=866

(lp3173

V<p>Here's a clip that aired last night on TV3.</p>\u000A<p>It shows NZ leading the world in our response to climate change in Bali. To quote the reporter, New Zealand is "...putting words into action... [announcing] ambitious plans to go carbon neutral".</p>\u000A\u000A\u000A\u000A<p>\u000A<p>National on the other hand has no credibility on climate change. They don't have any real answers. Many of them, including John Key, are climate-change deniers.</p>\u000A<p>As Phil Goff put it in this <a href="http://youtube.com/watch?v=F7k9LUV7szY">YouTube clip</a> four months ago, "There are two big issues facing the world. In terms of conflict - Iraq. In terms of wider issues it's about global warming. In both cases, John Key has got it wrong."</p>\u000A<p>Evidently Key's personal ambition doesn't stretch as far as helping to save the planet.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2007/09/28_large1.thumbnail.jpg" title="28_large1.jpg" alt="28_large1.jpg" height="72" hspace="5" width="50" /></p>\u000A<p><strong>\u201C[Climate change] is a complete and utter hoax.\u201D</strong><br />\u000A<em> (Hansard, 10 May 2005)</em></p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2007/09/billenglish.thumbnail.jpg" title="billenglish.jpg" alt="billenglish.jpg" height="71" hspace="5" width="50" /></p>\u000A<p><strong>\u201C[I\u2019m] quite worried that policies are going to be driven by this Armageddon mentality that the world has\u2026 far too much carbon.\u201D</strong><br />\u000A<em> (Investigate, Feb 2007)</em></p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2007/09/44_large.thumbnail.jpg" title="44_large.jpg" alt="44_large.jpg" height="68" hspace="5" width="50" /></p>\u000A<p><strong>\u201CI am a climate change sceptic. There I\u2019ve said it.\u201D</strong><br />\u000A<em> (Ashburton Guardian, 10 Nov 2006 )</em></p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2007/09/61_large.thumbnail.jpg" title="61_large.jpg" alt="61_large.jpg" height="72" hspace="5" width="50" /></p>\u000A<p><strong>\u201CI am not inclined to agree with the Government\u2019s view that there is a scientific consensus on climate change.\u201D</strong><br />\u000A<em> (Wairarapa News, 16 Aug 2006)</em></p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2007/09/26_large.thumbnail.jpg" title="26_large.jpg" alt="26_large.jpg" height="72" hspace="5" width="50" /></p>\u000A<p><strong>\u201CAs a politician I am not sure about this climate change story.\u201D</strong><br />\u000A<em> (Hansard, 17 Feb 2004)</em></p>\u000A<p class="akst_link"><a href="http://www.thestandard.org.nz/?p=866&amp;akst_action=share-this" title="E-mail this, post to del.icio.us, etc." id="akst_link_866" class="akst_share_link" rel="nofollow">Share This</a>\u000A</p>
